New Distribution of the Eastern Route Army's Bandit Suppression Efforts 104

The divisions in Fujian are formed into two columns.

To connect the Jiangxi armies into one line.

Lin Shouchang drank a bullet after being arrested and died.

Fuzhou Correspondence: After Jiang Dingwen, the former commander-in-chief of the Northern Route, was promoted to commander-in-chief of the Eastern Route, he has established a headquarters in Xiamen and abolished the Northern Front Headquarters in Fuzhou on the 21st, changed to the Office of the Eastern Route Headquarters stationed in the province. Jiang can go to Xiamen to take up the post in one or two days. The new commander of the Eastern Route Front, Wei Lihuang, also led his troops from Quanzhou through Datian Dehua to the northwest. Now Chairman Jiang has instructed Jiang Wei to lead the divisions in Fujian to clear the Red Bandits who are disrupting the border between Fujian and Jiangxi within a time limit. The current troops in Fujian include Li Yutang, Leng Xin, Li Yannian, Li Moan, Song Xilian, Lu Xingbang, Liu Heding, Chen Mingren, Liu Kan, Wang Jingjiu, Sun Yuanliang, Chen Qixuan, Zhou Zhiqun, and Zhang Luanji, a total of 14 divisions. There are eight divisions concentrated in northern Fujian, which Chairman Jiang has organized into two columns, which are advancing towards Shaxian, Yong'an, Shunchang and Jiangle, in order to respond to the two bandit suppression armies of Chen Cheng and Gu Zhutong on the Jiangxi border. Liu Heding is the commander of the Ninth Column, commanding the three divisions of Lu Xingbang, Zhou Zhiqun, and Zhang Luanji, and is in charge of the right wing. Tang Enbo is the commander of the Tenth Column, commanding the three divisions of Leng Xin, Chen Mingren, and Sun Yuanliang, and is in charge of the left wing. According to military information yesterday, the vanguard of Sun's division on the left wing has crossed Shunchang and is advancing towards Jiangle. The rear teams are also advancing from Yanping towards Shunchang. Liu's division on the right wing has launched an attack from Yanping towards Shaxian. The battle on the Qingzhou side is gradually becoming more intense. Most of the bandits are now in the Shayong area and are rushing to build fortifications in preparation for resistance. Only a small number of Red Guards are left in the Jiangshun area, and their strength is very weak. Therefore, the main battle will be in Shaxian. Once Shaxian is down, Jiangle will lose its support and can be defeated without a fight. According to the plan of the military authorities, the first phase of the operation is to recover the four counties of Shayong Jiangshun within a month, and the second phase is to advance to Mingxi, Qingliu, Jianning, and Taining, so as to form a line with the National Army in Jiangxi.

The issue of disbanding the civilian army was ordered by the Nanchang camp to be handled by Chen Yi and Xiao Qian, the director and deputy director of the Security Department. Regarding the disbandment standards, not only the strength of the army must be paid attention to, but also the past history of the leaders must be investigated. It is expected that personnel will be dispatched to check the troops within a few days. Lin Zhen (ie Lin Shouchang), the commander of the Second Route of the Fujian Anti-Rebellion People's Army, was recently arrested by the Security Department by order of the Nanchang Camp for a certain case and was detained at the headquarters of the Fourth Regiment of the Constitution in Qingduguan. At 4:00 AM on the 23rd, he died from a bullet in Donghu Camp. According to military sources, it was originally planned to be sent to Nanchang for interrogation. Because Lin tried to escape at night, the guards fired to stop him and was killed by a bullet. His family prepared a coffin and collected the body in the evening. Another piece of news, the Security Department yesterday issued a notice to the civilian armies of various routes to cut off and submit all seals to the department. During this disbandment period, they are absolutely not allowed to engage in external activities. After the reorganization into security regiments in the future, they will also be strictly trained by the sub-bureaus of each district to become local self-defense forces. (February 24th)

Kong Bandits Attempt to Disrupt the Nanchang-Xunyang Road 105

Crossing from Wuning to Tujiapu Station.

Being ambushed and dispersed by the National Army.

Jiujiang Communication: Kong bandits' pseudo Sixth Army Corps' pseudo Sixteenth Division, Seventeenth Division, and Red Third Division rioted from Yifeng to Fengxin Jing'an yesterday, and really had an attempt to disrupt the Nanchang-Xunyang Road. Originally, it was very close for the bandits to go from Anyi to Nanchang-Xunyang Road, but the bandits' cunning plan must be to flee from Wuning to the area bordering Ruichang and southern Hubei. Gu Baihuai's suspicion of fleeing back to his old nest in Yangxin, and then crossing the border between Wuning Ruichang and Dean, attacking Yongxiu along the Xiushui River, attempting to cut off the traffic on the Nanchang-Xunyang Road, and rob supplies. According to news from the transportation industry, Kong bandits' pseudo Sixteenth Division and Red Third Division, about 1,000 to 2,000 people, with hundreds of guns, fled from Yongxiu to the vicinity of Tujiapu Station on the Nanchang-Xunyang Road on the 25th, with the aim of destroying the railway tracks and bridges there, and robbing passenger cars. Fortunately, the local garrison Zhu Yaohua's division was prepared early and was engaged in blocking west of the railway line. At the same time, the troops advancing from Wuning to suppress the bandits also followed up and attacked. They were unsuccessful. At the moment, the bandits are still wandering around northern Jiangxi, without a definite purpose. The various troops of the Third Column Zhu Yue are using all their strength to launch guerrillas and blockades everywhere, and the bandits will have nowhere to flee. (February 27th)

Special item

First Draft of the Constitution of the Republic of China 111

Chapter 1 General Provisions

Article 1: The Republic of China is a republic based on the Three Principles of the People. Article 2: Sovereignty in the Republic of China resides in the people as a whole. Article 3: Those who possess the nationality of the Republic of China are citizens of the Republic of China. Article 4: The territory of the Republic of China includes the domains of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, Sichuan, Xikang, Hebei, Shandong, Shanxi, Henan, Shaanxi, Gansu, Qinghai, Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, Chahar, Suiyuan, Ningxia, Xinjiang, Mongolia and Tibet. The territory of the Republic of China shall not be altered save by resolution of the National Congress. Administrative divisions and regional names shall be prescribed by law. Article 5: The capital of the Republic of China shall be Nanjing. Article 6: The national flag of the Republic of China shall be a blue sky and white sun on a red ground.

Article 2 Rights and Duties of the People 112

Article 7: All citizens of the Republic of China, regardless of gender, race, religion, class, or occupation, are equal before the law. Article 8: People have the freedom of their person. They shall not be arrested, detained, interrogated, or punished except in accordance with the law. If a person is arrested or detained on suspicion of committing a crime, the executing agency shall inform the person and their relatives of the reasons for the execution within 24 hours at the latest and transfer them to the competent court for interrogation. The person or others may also petition the competent court to request the executing agency to bring the person in for interrogation within 24 hours. The court shall not refuse the foregoing petition, and the executing agency shall not refuse the court's request for interrogation. Article 9: People shall not be subject to military trials except for those in active military service. Article 10: People have the freedom of residence, and their residences shall not be violated, searched, or sealed except in accordance with the law. Article 11: People have the freedom of movement, which shall not be suspended or restricted except in accordance with the law. Article 12: People have the freedom of assembly and association, which shall not be suspended or restricted except in accordance with the law. Article 13: People have the freedom of speech, writing, and publication, which shall not be suspended or restricted except in accordance with the law. Article 14: People have the freedom of secret communication, which shall not be suspended or restricted except in accordance with the law. Article 15: People have the freedom of religious belief, which shall not be restricted except in accordance with the law. Article 16: People's property shall not be requisitioned, confiscated, sealed, or confiscated except in accordance with the law. Article 17: People have the right to petition, appeal, and sue in accordance with the law. Article 18: People have the right to elect, recall, initiate, and referendum in accordance with the law. Article 19: People have the right to take examinations in accordance with the law. Article 20: People have the obligation to pay taxes in accordance with the law. Article 21: People have the obligation to perform military service and corvée in accordance with the law. Article 22: People have the obligation to serve in public office in accordance with the law. Article 23: Any laws that suspend or restrict the freedom or rights of the people shall be limited to what is necessary for social order and public interest.

Article 3 National Economy 113

Article 24: The State shall establish an economic system based on the Principle of People's Livelihood, improve the production, distribution, and consumption of wealth, in order to achieve an equitable livelihood for the people. Article 25: Land within the territory of the Republic of China belongs to the entire people. The ownership of land acquired by the people in accordance with the law shall be protected and restricted by law. Landowners have the obligation to fully utilize the land they own. Article 26: Minerals attached to the land and natural forces that are economically available for public use belong to the State and shall not be affected by the people's acquisition of land ownership. Article 27: The value of land that increases without the application of labor and capital shall be for the public benefit of the people. The method of making the land appreciation for the public enjoyment of the people is to collect land appreciation tax. Article 28: The State shall allocate and organize land to support self-cultivating farmers and those who use land themselves as a principle. Article 29: In order to improve the distribution of wealth, the state shall adopt the following measures: 1. Levy income tax and inheritance tax at progressive tax rates; 2. Formulate a reasonable surplus distribution system to balance the economic interests of labor and capital; 3. Restrict private capital lending interest and real estate use rent; 4. Level the prices of food and other necessities of life; 5. Promote various cooperative enterprises. Article 30: In order to improve the living conditions of workers, the state shall implement a policy of protecting workers. Women and children engaged in labor should be given special protection according to their age and physical condition. Article 31: Both labor and capital should develop production enterprises based on the principle of coordination and mutual benefit. Article 32: The state shall provide appropriate relief and compensation to people who are disabled or die due to military service, corvée, and public service. Article 33: In order to develop the rural economy, the government should actively implement the following items: 1. Reclaim wasteland and develop farmland water conservancy; 2. Establish agricultural financial institutions to encourage rural cooperative enterprises; 3. Implement the warehouse system to prevent famines and enrich people's food; 4. Develop agricultural education and improve farmers' lives; 5. Improve rural housing and build rural roads.

Article 4 National Education 114

Article 34: The Three Principles of the People are the fundamental principles of national education in the Republic of China. Article 35: All citizens of the Republic of China have equal opportunities to receive education. Article 36: Education should aim to cultivate noble character, enhance life skills, and create sound citizens. Article 37: Children of school age should all receive compulsory education. People who have not received compulsory education should all receive adult literacy education. Article 38: All public and private educational institutions in the country are subject to state supervision and have the obligation to promote the educational policies set by the state. Article 39: National universities and national vocational schools should focus on the needs of the region in order to maintain equal opportunities for people in all regions to enjoy higher education and promote the balanced development of national culture. Article 40: The minimum amount of education funding should be 15% of its total budget at the central level and 30% of its total budget at the local level. Its legally independent education fund should also be guaranteed. Article 41: Private schools with excellent performance should be rewarded and subsidized. Article 42: Overseas Chinese education should be rewarded and subsidized. Article 43: All public and private schools across the country set up free and scholarship places to reward students with excellent moral and academic character who cannot afford to go to school. Article 44: Teachers and staff with excellent performance and long service should be rewarded and protected. Article 45: Those who have made inventions in academic research should be rewarded and protected. Article 46: Historical sites and cultural relics related to history, culture, and art should be protected or preserved by the state.

Chapter Five: The National Assembly 115

Article 47: The National Assembly shall be composed of representatives elected in accordance with the following methods: 1. One representative shall be elected from each county or city and areas equivalent thereto. Areas equivalent to counties or cities shall be determined by law. 2. The number of representatives elected by the people of Mongolia and Tibet shall be determined by law. 3. The number of representatives elected by citizens of the Republic of China residing abroad shall be determined by law. Article 48: The election of representatives to the National Assembly shall be conducted by universal, equal, direct, and secret ballot. Article 49: Citizens of the Republic of China who have reached the age of twenty shall have the right to elect representatives in accordance with the law, and those who have reached the age of twenty-five shall have the right to be elected as representatives in accordance with the law. Article 50: The National Assembly shall be convened once every three years, and each session shall be limited to one month. Article 51: The functions of the National Assembly are as follows: 1. To elect and recall the President, Vice President, members of the Legislative Yuan, members of the Control Yuan, the President and Vice President of the Judicial Yuan, and the President and Vice President of the Examination Yuan, and to impeach the Premier of the Executive Yuan. 2. To initiate legislative principles. 3. To ratify laws. 4. To enact and amend the Constitution. 5. To receive reports from the National Government. 6. To handle matters submitted by the National Government for resolution. 7. Other powers conferred by this Constitution. Article 52: Representatives of the National Assembly shall not be held responsible to the outside world for speeches and votes made during meetings. Article 53: Representatives of the National Assembly shall not be arrested or imprisoned during sessions without the permission of the National Assembly, except in cases of being caught in the act of committing a crime. Article 54: The powers of the representatives of the National Assembly shall terminate on the day the session is closed. Article 55: During the adjournment of the National Assembly, a National Committee shall be established, consisting of twenty-one members and ten alternate members, who shall be elected by the National Assembly. The members and alternate members mentioned in the preceding paragraph shall not be limited to representatives of the National Assembly. Article 56: The members and alternate members of the National Committee shall possess the following qualifications: 1. Being at least forty-five years of age. 2. Having special meritorious service and outstanding virtue for the nation. 3. Having made significant contributions to politics or academia. Article 57: Members of the National Committee shall not hold other positions concurrently. Article 58: The functions of the National Committee are as follows: 1. To take over the Secretariat of the National Assembly after the adjournment of the Assembly and prepare for the convening of the next Assembly. 2. To convene a temporary National Assembly upon the request of the National Government or when the Control Yuan impeaches the President or Vice President and the resolution is passed by more than three-fourths of the members. 3. To handle impeachment cases by the Control Yuan against the Presidents and Vice Presidents of the Executive Yuan, Judicial Yuan, and Examination Yuan, as well as members of the Legislative Yuan and members of the Control Yuan. 4. To handle the Legislative Yuan's vote of no confidence in the Premier of the Executive Yuan. 5. Other powers conferred by this Constitution. Article 59: The organization and election of the National Assembly, as well as the organization and election of the National Committee, shall be determined by law.

Chapter Six: The Powers of the Central and Local Governments 116

Article 60: The central and local governments shall adopt a system of balanced powers. Matters of a national nature shall be assigned to the central government, and matters that should be adapted to local conditions shall be assigned to local governments. Article 61: The power to legislate on the following matters belongs to the central government: 1. Nationality. 2. Civil Law, Criminal Law, and Procedural Law. 3. Judiciary. 4. Examinations. 5. Control. 6. National Defense and Military System. 7. Foreign Affairs. 8. Household Registration. 9. Local Political System. 10. Garrison and Public Security. 11. Education and Culture. 12. Public Health, Epidemic Prevention, and Medicine. 13. Calendar, Weights and Measures, and other calculation systems that should be uniformly prescribed nationwide. 14. Finance and Financial Supervision. 15. Monetary System and National Bank. 16. State-owned monopolies and other state-owned economic enterprises. 17. Land System. 18. Labor System. 19. Postal Service, Telegraph, and other water, land, and air transportation or transportation enterprises. 20. National Engineering, Water Conservancy, and construction matters related to the whole country. 21. Trademarks, Patents, Licenses, and other economic rights that should be uniformly prescribed nationwide. 22. Banking, Insurance, and other financial enterprises. 23. Mining, Forestry, and Fisheries. 24. Overseas Chinese Affairs. 25. Immigration and Colonization. 26. Other matters that should be uniformly prescribed nationwide. Article 62: Matters not listed in the preceding article may be subject to separate regulations by local governments or to principles prescribed by the central government for local governments to formulate regulations, but local regulations that conflict with central laws shall be invalid. Article 63: The land, sea, and air forces of the entire country shall be conscripted and trained by the central government in accordance with the law. Article 64: The division of taxation between the central and local governments and the methods of financial assistance or subsidies shall be determined by law. Article 65: The revenue and expenditure of the central and local governments shall be compiled into a general budget and a general final account once every fiscal year, and the scope and procedures for their compilation shall be determined by law. The compilation of the operating budgets and final accounts of public enterprises of the central and local governments may be governed by separate laws, but their net profits and losses shall still be incorporated into the general budget and general final account in accordance with the law. Article 66: The financial organization of all government agencies, its treasury, accounting, and auditing departments shall each maintain its independence.

Chapter Seven: The Central Political System 117

Section 1: The National Government Article 67: The National Government shall exercise the administrative power, legislative power, judicial power, examination power, and control power of the Republic of China. Article 68: The National Government shall be organized by the President and the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Examination Yuan, and Control Yuan. Article 69: The President and the five Yuans shall each be responsible to the National Assembly. Article 70: Laws and orders shall be promulgated by the National Government, signed by the President in accordance with the law, and countersigned by the head of the competent Yuan. Article 71: The National Government shall command the land, sea, and air forces. Article 72: The National Government shall exercise the power to declare war, make peace, and conclude treaties. Article 73: The National Government shall declare and lift martial law. Article 74: The National Government shall exercise the power of amnesty, special pardon, commutation of sentence, and restoration of rights. Article 75: The National Government shall confer honors. Article 76: The heads of the five Yuans may issue orders in accordance with the law.

Regulations for Taxing Parcels Sent by Mail 126

Procedures Will Change Starting April 1st

According to postal sources, the existing regulations for taxing parcels sent by mail will undergo changes starting on April 1st of this year. All parcels handed over to inland bureaus within this district for dispatch to inland bureaus in other districts that are not directly connected by train and do not have customs personnel stationed there must, from that day onwards, undergo the procedure of having the contents inspected and taxed by customs officers of this administration. If the inspection and taxation have not been carried out by customs officers of this administration, the final bureau through which the parcel passes and where customs personnel are stationed will still have to go through the above-mentioned inspection and taxation procedures.

Mechanical Industry Association Submits a Request for Interpretation of the "Knowledge" in Trademark Law 127

The Shanghai Mechanical Chinese Products Factory Joint Association submitted a request to the Supreme Court yesterday for an interpretation of the meaning of the word "knowledge" in Article 2, Paragraph 6 of the Trademark Law, as it is considered ambiguous. The original text reads, "Submitted for the interpretation of similarity and resemblance in trademark law. We believe that the so-called 'mark known to the world' in Article 2, Paragraph 6 of the Trademark Law, does the word 'knowledge' include the word 'recognition'? We would like to request an interpretation to avoid disputes. The two words 'knowledge' and 'discussion' are often used together, but in reality, there is quite a difference between them. For example, Paragraphs 1 and 3 of the same article are all discussed by those who have eyes, for fear that people will not know the truth and therefore misunderstand. Therefore, even similar ones should be prohibited. Those without eyes cannot know what the shape of the graphic symbol is to use for recognition. It can be asserted. However, most of the marks known to the world are bought by name. They only know one thing, but not the other. For example, the Triangle Brand towel and the Invincible Brand toothpaste have become known to the world after decades of advertising. Even blind people know that they never deceive the public. Some people pass it on by word of mouth and ask others to buy it on their behalf. Some have known its name for a long time but have never seen it. Knowing but not recognizing is like someone asking for directions, knowing the name of the destination but not recognizing the words. If there are similar places in singing and calling, wouldn't it mislead people? Therefore, when the Trademark Law was first formulated, there was also a considerable discussion on singing and calling in the translation of foreign statutory law. Now, does the word 'knowledge' in Article 2, Paragraph 6 of the Trademark Law include knowledge in the heart? If someone maliciously uses the same sound but different characters to insinuate a trademark known to the world, such as applying for registration of 'British Dan Commander' to use on the same type of goods as 'Indanthrene Blue', can it be allowed? Or can't different merchants use such similar trademarks? This matter concerns legal precedents, so we should submit a request for interpretation to prevent opportunism and eliminate the trend of deception. This is in the public interest."

Owners of Adjacent Properties to the Government's Sand Field Property Given Priority to Increase Lease and Extend Deadline by Two Months 128

Land Bureau Posted a Notice Yesterday

In order to protect the property rights of the property owners adjacent to the government's sand field property, the Municipal Land Bureau had stipulated a deadline for the owners to increase their leases with priority. However, due to the short deadline, it was feared that the owners would not have enough time to apply for the increase. Therefore, the bureau extended the deadline by another two months so that the owners could leisurely apply for the increase or add rent. Yesterday, Special Announcement No. 97 was issued, which read, "After the municipality recovered the government's sand field property in the city and managed it independently, the disposal methods were previously stipulated to allow adjacent property owners or current occupants to increase their leases with priority. The owners of the adjacent permanent lease deeds can also request to add rent to the deed. Now that the deadline has expired, many applications have been received by the bureau. However, the municipality has a vast territory, and there are many who have not yet applied, possibly due to the short deadline and insufficient time. It is important to know that this sand field property is closely related to the property rights of the adjacent property owners. Once the priority lease increase period has passed and a third party applies for the lease, it will have a considerable impact on the use of the original land. Therefore, as a matter of seriousness, the deadline is extended by another two months, until April 30th of this year, as the deadline for priority lease increase for adjacent property owners, etc. Those who wish to increase the lease or add rent to the adjacent beaches, wasteland, and wharves must submit their applications to the bureau within the deadline or submit them through the consular office in charge. After this deadline expires, others will be allowed to apply for the lease freely, and no further extensions will be granted. Afterwards, the owners or tenants of the adjacent properties must not raise any objections or obstruct the process. In addition to reporting to the municipal government for record-keeping and separately notifying all parties, a notice is hereby issued for compliance."

The Consuls General of fourteen countries stationed in Shanghai, including Kenneth Cantine, the U.S. Consul General, issued a proclamation yesterday regarding the election of directors of the Public Works Department and members of the Real Estate Committee. The proclamation stated, "In accordance with Article 9 and Article 6A of the Shanghai Public Concession Land Regulations, the election of directors of the Public Works Department for the 1934 municipal year and the election of one Real Estate Committee member for the same year by registered landowners in the Public Concession are scheduled to be held on Monday, March 26th, and Tuesday, March 27th of this year. Ballots must be submitted to the Public Works Department for verification no later than 12:00 noon on Saturday, March 17th of this year. This proclamation is issued for general information." Signed by: Kenneth Cantine, U.S. Consul General; Olle Reen, Norwegian Consul General; de Kroman, Dutch Consul General; Sir John Brenan, British Consul General; John Rothe, Danish Consul General; Varela, Spanish Consul General; Silfa, Portuguese Consul General; Ratt, Swiss Consul General; Meria, French Consul General; Ishisha, Japanese Consul General; Lindquist, Swedish Consul General; Narone, Italian Consul General; de la Four, Belgian Chargé d'Affaires; Almeida, Brazilian Consul.

Stirling Fessenden, Director General of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, also issued two proclamations yesterday, which are recorded as follows: (1) Proclamation regarding the election of directors of this Bureau for the 1934 municipal year and the election of one Real Estate Committee member for the same year by registered landowners in the Public Concession. The elections are scheduled to be held on Monday, March 26th, and Tuesday, March 27th. Ballots must be submitted to the Director General of this Bureau for verification no later than 12:00 noon on Saturday, March 17th. This proclamation is issued for general information. (2) Proclamation regarding the list of those entitled to vote at this year's Taxpayers' Annual Meeting, which was revised to December 1, 1933, and published in the Bureau's Gazette on December 5, 1933, in accordance with Article 19 of the Land Regulations. If there are any errors or omissions, please send a notice to the Chief of the Finance Office and Director of the Donation Division, No. 209 Jiangxi Road, Office of the Director General of this Bureau for verification. To facilitate the preparation of the voter list, all those who are entitled to vote in the election of directors at this year's meeting are requested to pay all taxes due by the deadline. This proclamation is issued for general information.

161st Meeting

It was decided to reply to the association that since lawyer Guo Qiming, a member of this association, was proceeding according to law, this association would provide legal assistance. (7) There are many law offices in this city, and there are some malpractices among them. Should methods be devised to ban them? It was decided to investigate and ban them. (8) The applications for membership from lawyers Hu Rihua, Chen Yaxuan, Wang Dekui, etc. It was decided to pass them and report them to courts at all levels for record purposes. After the discussions, it was already late at night, so the meeting was adjourned.

After the Increase in Prices of Sichuan Steamers, the Transportation of Chinese Goods to Sichuan Will Be Blocked 135

The Sichuan Business Group Dealing in Foreign Sundries Changed to Transporting Domestic Products

The Increase in Freight Rates Creates Opportunities for the Dumping of Japanese Goods

The Group Decided to Send Representatives to Petition Society

The Sichuan River steamers' alliance to raise prices and the resulting backlash from the Sichuan business community has been reported in this newspaper. The most affected are the business groups dealing in foreign sundries. However, although this group is called "foreign sundries", they have completely switched to selling domestic products in recent years. This time, the increase in prices of the Sichuan steamers is unreasonable, with some freight rates even exceeding the cost of the goods, which will make it impossible for the industry to operate. Now that appeals have been ineffective, it has been decided to petition the Social Affairs Bureau. The reporter went to various parties yesterday to investigate and provide the details as follows.

Unfair Rate Agreement 136

The Sichuan steamer alliance increased fees in the name of saving the shipping industry, increasing water feet, and maintaining costs. However, when representatives of the various shipping companies were negotiating new cargo prices, a Chinese person named Li and a Russian person drafted the water feet and increased the water feet for foreign sundries (which are actually all domestic products, with no foreign goods) to more than the cost of the goods, and charged by gross measurement. This kind of unreasonable new water feet, once implemented, will wipe out the domestic goods transported and sold to Sichuan, making it impossible to operate. The group once publicly discussed requesting a modification of this freight rate to show fairness, but was rejected by the shipping bureau.

New Prices Exceed the Cost of Goods 137

The so-called "foreign general merchandise" includes enamelware, toothbrushes, silk stockings, thermos bottles, glass cups, children's toys, stainless steel utensils, bakelite bowls and saucers, as well as toothpaste, lanterns, and other such items. These are numerous and varied, and all are manufactured by our own factories. Last year, these domestic goods were sold at low prices, and many were shipped to Sichuan. In the shipping companies' freight bills, they were all listed under the category of "foreign general merchandise." In reality, the cost is not high. For example, a box occupying 30 square feet of space would have a value of only sixty or seventy yuan. This is because most of these goods take up a lot of space. Now, the new freight rates for Sichuan-bound ships have increased to eighty yuan per ton. With each ton calculated at forty cubic feet, the shipping cost for one box of goods would be sixty yuan. Furthermore, fees are collected by size, regardless of gross or net weight. In practice, the freight cost is even greater than the value of the goods.

Domestic Goods Unable to Be Transported to Sichuan 138

The "foreign general merchandise" industry believes that this new freight rate will make it impossible to transport domestic goods to Sichuan. Even if the price of goods is moderately increased due to the high freight costs, it is impossible to raise the price of one yuan goods to two yuan. This price increase clearly cuts off the operating path for those dealing in domestic goods. At a time when Japanese goods are seeking to dump their products on the market, this is nothing short of creating an excellent opportunity for them. This is because Japanese goods utilize their own country's ships to promote sales upstream along the Yangtze River in a continuous stream. The result will be not only significant losses for the Sichuan "foreign general merchandise" industry, but also a blow to domestic goods.

Request for Relief for the People's Livelihood 139

Tai Koo, Jardine Matheson, and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company are foreign businesses, so the current price increase is somewhat understandable. However, the Minsheng Company, which has the most ships and the greatest influence in the Sichuan River, and which advocates for the principle of people's livelihood, is a Chinese business. It should be providing assistance for the transport of domestic goods to Sichuan. Yet, when the freight rates were revised, it was the representative of this company who proposed the increase. They only considered the increase in freight rates, and not the suffering of the people's livelihood. This is especially painful to the industry. Currently, the Sichuan "foreign general merchandise" industry, in addition to having already stopped ordering goods, has decided to elect representatives to petition the Social Affairs Bureau to suppress this unreasonable freight rate and prevent the nascent domestic goods industry from suffering a significant setback. The petition is already being drafted and will be submitted immediately.

Creating a Situation Where Others Reap the Benefits 140

A total of seven shipping companies have joined the agreement to raise rates for Sichuan routes. However, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has not joined because its ship, the "Mount Emei," ran aground and is not in operation. In addition, the Nissin Company did not join the alliance. After the rate increase, the Chekiang Second Ship "Yiping" and the Minsheng Second Ship "Minkang" left port yesterday with only a small amount of cotton yarn. Not a single piece of general merchandise was on board. The two sides are in a standoff. Japanese ships are planning to take this opportunity to resume navigation on the Sichuan River. They are not bound by the agreement and can freely adjust freight rates to stir up trouble. At that time, the "foreign general merchandise" industry will inevitably load onto Japanese ships due to their lower freight rates. This is the result of the Minsheng Company and others. When the snipe and clam fight, the fisherman profits. It is a truly painful matter.

Owners of McGill Road Apartments Cut Off Water Yesterday Due to Water Fee Dispute 143

Notice Issued Seeking Assistance

According to the New Sound News Agency, the tenants of McGill Road apartments, after receiving a notice from the owner, the Ewo Bank, on the 26th of last month, giving them 24 hours to pay the water fees, all decided to abide by last year's court decision and stop paying the water fees due to the owner's unreasonable demands. At the same time, they also convened a meeting to discuss countermeasures. Yesterday (the 1st), the owner's side acted according to the letter, sending two foreigners and one Chinese to the apartments and cutting off the water supply to all the tenants. They also posted notices to attract tenants, as a warning. The rent reduction association of the apartments convened an emergency meeting yesterday to discuss the matter. The results were: (1) notify members to withhold water fees and wait for a resolution; (2) file a lawsuit according to law; (3) request assistance from the rent reduction committee due to the owner's unreasonable oppression. However, the owner, Ewo Bank, sent a letter to the New Sound News Agency, clarifying that the court had not rejected their claims. The tenants' notice and the owner's original letter are recorded separately below.

Tenants' Notice 144

Notice from the McGill Road Branch of the First Special District of the Shanghai Rent Reduction Committee: Regarding the matter of the notice, it has been found that the landlord of this apartment building previously increased the water fee by two yuan per household, causing all 400+ residents to rise up in opposition. Zhong Delin, Wu Jiaxiang, Jin Derong, and others argued reasonably and resisted. They went to court on August 12th of last year and the court ruled that the owner's unreasonable increase of the water fee by two yuan was inconsistent with the water company's regulations and rejected the floating collection in court. Subsequently, the owner disregarded public reason and violated the law, still collecting two yuan per household, and cutting off the water pipes if payment was delayed, disregarding the livelihood of the people and ignoring the drinking water of the community. This committee, out of concern for the general welfare of the working class, has specially sent a document to the general committee requesting assistance. In addition, all residents are required to pay the rent as usual, but to unanimously withhold the additional two yuan for the water fee, and wait for this committee to file a lawsuit in accordance with the law, and wait for a solution. This notice is given to ensure everyone is aware.

Letter to the Rent Reduction Committee 145

The preparatory committee of the rent reduction branch of the apartment building sent a letter to the rent reduction committee requesting assistance: Respectfully, our committee is in its initial stage of preparation and many matters are pending. Suddenly, residents Zhong Delin, Wu Jiaxiang, Jin Derong, and others came to the committee to report that the owner of the building sent two foreigners and two Chinese to collect water fees of two yuan per household, aggressively demanding payment, and cutting off the water pipes of those who could not afford to pay (three families), disregarding the drinking water of the community and ignoring the people's livelihood to the extreme. According to the investigation, the water fee was increased by two yuan not before the lease began, but after the lease was already in effect. This had already caused the residents to rise up in opposition. On August 12th of last year, the special district court ruled that the owner's floating collection was unreasonable and completely inconsistent with the water company's regulations, and rejected the floating collection in court. Now the owner is using the collection of water fees as an excuse for intentional provocation. We are specially submitting a document to the general committee requesting assistance in accordance with the law in order to reassure the public. This is truly a matter of public concern.

Owner's Statement 146

Ewo Bank, the owner of the apartments, sent a letter to the New Sound News Agency yesterday, stating: Respectfully, I read the article "Owner of McGill Road Apartments Causes Repercussions by Limiting Water Fee Payments" in the local news section of the newspaper on the 25th. The content of the article published by your agency is not in accordance with the facts. The McGill Road water fee is based on a contract between the water company and the owner, which collects 7.5% of the rent. Therefore, the owner also collects the water fee from the tenants at 7.5% of the rent and merges it with the rent. Since May of last year, the water company suddenly changed its rules and ordered the owner to install water meters and collect fees based on the actual amount of water consumed. After implementation, the water fee expenditure has increased by more than two times. The owner's losses are too great, and we were forced to send a letter to each tenant in July, notifying them that we would increase the water fee by three yuan per household in order to subsidize the losses. We also stated that if tenants did not want to pay the increased water fee, they could install their own water meters, which would be fair. Later, the joint office of the tenants of the apartments sent a letter expressing their understanding, but requested that starting in August of the 22nd year, they would agree to pay an additional water fee of two yuan per month per household. The owner, for the sake of mutual understanding, reluctantly accepted, and did not take into account the losses for June and July. Subsequently, more than 100 tenants in the apartments have been paying the monthly fees as agreed. However, three tenants, Zhong Delin, Jin Derong, and Wu Jiaxiang, have violated the unanimous public opinion of the joint office and insisted on refusing to pay. Despite repeated persuasion, they have refused to listen. As of December of last year, in addition to the unpaid water fees, Zhong and Wu also owed several months of rent. The owner initially requested mediation from the court, but the mediation failed because the opposing party disagreed. Subsequently, a lawsuit was filed. Regarding the water fee portion, the court stated that since the defendant had not agreed, a separate lawsuit was required. The news report stating that the court had rejected the floating collection is clearly not true. As for the notice of deadline for payment of water fees the day before yesterday, it was only for these very few three households, and not all tenants received the notice. The truth of the matter still awaits a legal resolution, but the inaccuracies in the report should be corrected. Therefore, the true facts of the matter are hereby communicated to your agency, and we request that you publish a correction in order to restore credibility. Thank you very much. Ewo Bank, Shanghai.

Overview of the Shanghai Wharf Affairs Office's Compilation of Work 147

Since the Shanghai Wharf Affairs Office was officially established in the winter of the 21st year by order of the Central Government, it has appropriately handled all disputes between labor and contractor businesses in the city's various wharves. The most important of these include resolving the disputes between the workers of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Bureau warehouse in Pudong and the split accounting heads, the disputes between the workers of the Yongchang warehouse in Pudong and the split accounting heads, and the disputes between the workers of the Dada Wharf and Datong warehouse and the contractors. A mediation decision was signed for each of these cases to ensure mutual adherence. As for other wharf disputes, the office handles several cases every day, and the office manages to resolve them and eliminate major disputes between labor and contractors invisibly, which greatly assists social security. As for charitable projects, such as the establishment of labor schools and workers' clubs, they provide wharf workers with a good opportunity to receive education. Currently, the office, in view of the fact that the outside world has not fully understood its work, has specially compiled a book summarizing its work from the date of its establishment to the end of December of the 22nd year. The content is rich and contains many important statistics related to the city's various wharves. It is said that this summary of work will be printed soon. It is expected that after it is printed, anyone concerned about the city's wharf business will have a good reference.

Drafting a Work Plan 148

Since its establishment, the Shanghai Wharf Affairs Office has spared no effort in handling all business matters between labor and contractors in the city's wharves. The office has now drafted a work plan for this year, which includes organization, mediation, welfare, and statistics. The plan includes conducting registration and organizing wharf labor unions and branch offices, establishing training classes for cadres and workers, promoting wharf workers' clubs, preparing for workers' savings and mutual assistance associations, adding worker's supplementary schools, workers' children's schools, establishing wharf workers' consumer cooperatives, and other matters. The office is now instructing the guidance section to intensify its work and proceed separately. After this plan is implemented, the city's wharf workers will receive many benefits.

Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Sends Letter to Customs to Stop Eviction of Firewood Boats from Dongjiadu 150

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs yesterday, stating: With respect, the firewood and charcoal industry association members' cargo ships in the city are moored in the area south of Dongjiadu at the location designated by the Public Works Bureau Wharf Management Office. Recently, they have been arbitrarily evicted by the customs patrol boats, which has hindered business and caused panic among the public. The association requested negotiation with the Chamber of Commerce. On the 23rd of this month, we forwarded a letter of complaint to your office, requesting you to instruct the relevant agency not to take action in order to maintain the livelihood of the people. On the 28th of this month, we received a follow-up letter from the association stating that, according to reports from various colleagues, not only has the customs patrol boat not stopped the eviction, but the suppression has intensified, ordering ship owners to moor at customs-designated locations. In view of this, after investigation, we believe that the Jianghai Customs patrol boats are so hostile to our cargo ships and interfere so greatly that the public is in constant fear. If this causes a strike among ship merchants, it will have a great impact on the fuel supply of residents and the social stability. Therefore, we urgently request that you quickly find a way to negotiate with the Jianghai Customs and prevent the situation from escalating.

Officially Started Yesterday

Traffic is heavy and frequent, making traffic maintenance difficult. Therefore, the Municipal Public Security Bureau has set up a red and green traffic light in the center of each road to maintain order. Red Cross Society Recruitment of Members Opened Yesterday 152

The Chinese Red Cross Society's membership recruitment convention opened yesterday. It is scheduled to host a banquet for the captains of the various teams at the Dadong Restaurant at 6:00 PM today. In recent days, the radio stations have been broadcasting the general idea that "Everyone has an important report now, please pay special attention to all circles, that is, the Chinese Red Cross Society, has been founded for 30 years. The number of people who have helped the people and rescued soldiers is no less than tens of millions. It is not only the leader of the charity circles in the country, but also won a lot of glory in the international arena. Now the Red Cross Society is ordered by the Ministry of the Interior, from March 1 to April 30, as the period for recruiting members. Today is the first day of the opening ceremony. I hope that all circles will enthusiastically participate, so as to fulfill the obligations that nationals should fulfill in the international arena, so that China's charitable status in the international arena will increase day by day. Because in the Eastern countries, like Siam, the population is about 8 million and there are more than 90,000 members. The Red Cross Society of Japan has about 3.88 million members, accounting for 20% of the national population. China is known as 400 million compatriots, and only 100,000 have joined the club, which is inevitably dwarfed, making the world think that the Chinese are less charitable than friendly countries. Therefore, the Chinese Red Cross Society wants to expand its business in rescue, disaster relief, treatment, and health in times of war and peace, so that all compatriots in the country can be safely guaranteed. Now, during the solicitation period, please ask the compassionate compatriots to quickly join the Red Cross Society. I think all philanthropists will certainly do what is right and not give in to benevolence. The General Assembly of the Red Cross Society is at No. 42 Jiujiang Road in Shanghai, and their branch is set up in more than 500 places in provinces, cities and counties. Please go to the nearby to connect with the treatment, and if you want to know the rank of members, you can ask the Red Cross Society to read the rules and regulations.

One Person Arrested and Taken to Bureau for Trial in Yangshupu Wharf Worker Conflict Case 153

The Rongji Company contracted the loading and unloading work at the Sino-American Petroleum Company warehouse in Yangshupu Wharf, Pudong on January 1 of this year. On the 10th of last month, the work began for the first time. Unexpectedly, while the work was in progress, more than 100 people resembling workers suddenly came forward to stop the work, resulting in a conflict. As a result, both sides were injured. A lawsuit was once filed, but altercations occurred repeatedly when work was done later on, and the company sent people to try their best to persuade them to temporarily maintain peace. However, rumors were rampant for a while, and everyone said that if the Rongji Company did not stop working, a bloody tragedy would inevitably occur. So Rongji heard the news and asked the Municipal Public Security Bureau to prevent it. On the 26th of last month, Director Wen ordered Pei Chengzong, the captain of the third squadron of the police corps, to lead more than a dozen police officers to be stationed there. However, at about 3:00 PM the following day (27th), 16 Rongji workers were unloading goods at the wharf when about 200 workers, each wearing a red cloth, came to the wharf together and forced them to stop working. At that time, Captain Pei, seeing the situation, urgently explained the importance of the situation to the crowd, persuading them to send representatives to come up with reasonable reasons to discuss calmly, and not to disrupt public order, which would cause inconvenience. The workers temporarily elected seven people to talk to Pei. The workers insisted on stopping work immediately before they could discuss, but the Sino-American Company believed that kerosene was very dangerous and time was of the essence, so the two sides could not come to an agreement. Immediately, more than 200 people caused a riot and rushed into the wharf together. The police tried to stop them, but there were a large number of workers, and the momentum was like a tide. At the same time, someone in the crowd shouted and beat them. In an instant, wooden sticks and iron rulers were raised together, and they knocked down squad leader Fu Jichuan, police officer Xu Jingren, and Miao Jingshan, and beat them severely. They also seized the gun shells from the police officers. Captain Pei tried his best to avoid escalating the situation, but the situation was very dangerous. For the sake of self-defense, the police fired empty shots into the sky as a warning, but at the same time, several gunshots occurred in the crowd. Suddenly, the order was disrupted, and the workers dispersed from all sides. At this time, Captain Fu's arm had been injured, and squad leader Fu Qingchuan, police officer Xu Jingren, and Miao Jingshan were all seriously injured and groaned on the ground. On the worker's side, three people were also injured by gunfire. The company urgently used the telephone to notify the nearby Sacred Heart Hospital on Ningguo Road to send an ambulance to send the injured people to the hospital for treatment. Captain Pei urgently reported to Director Wen and asked for instructions. It was said that of the three injured workers, except for two who were not in critical condition, the other was in critical condition. According to the results of the investigation by the Public Security Bureau, most of the gunshots were believed to be pistol bullets. However, the police officers sent there were all using box cannons and long guns, so they paid close attention to this matter and feared that disruptors were inciting trouble from the middle, so they planned to investigate thoroughly. Unexpectedly, the next day, Captain Pei suddenly ran into one of the seven representatives at the Yangshupu small vegetable market and arrested him. He was handed over to the nearby gang and taken to the police station. He was escorted to the First Special Court yesterday. According to the confession, his name is Han Dexin, from Shandong. The rest of the words were vague. Han requested bail in court, but the police station found that Han had been sentenced to imprisonment in the boundary. The police lawyer objected to bail. Captain Pei stated in court that Han had committed a crime in the court at the time. The Public Security Bureau sent someone to request that the court allow him to be taken to the court. Han was handed over to the staff and taken back to the case for trial.

Minutes of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce Industrial Research Meeting 154

Industrial Production Control Regulations Passed

The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce convened the fifth meeting of the Industrial and Commercial Research Association at 3:00 PM the day before yesterday. The members Hu Xiyuan, Hu Juewen, Zheng Chengqing, Yang Qingqing, Jin Runxiang, Chen Xiaodie (representing Yang), Lu Wenshao, and Zhu Wenqi (representing Zheng) and others attended. His Mother Passed Away, and the Encoffining Ceremony Will Be Held Today

Sun Pu Will Temporarily Take Over the Bureau's Affairs

Municipal Public Security Bureau Director Wen Hongen's mother, 73 years old, had been suffering from a cough recently. She passed away from a severe illness at 11:30 AM the day before yesterday. The coffin will be temporarily stored at the funeral home and the date of the funeral will be chosen later. National Art Academy Exhibition Opens Tomorrow Morning 156

The National Hangzhou Art Academy is scheduled to display various products of the school and hold an exhibition at No. 11 Huanlong Road from March 3rd to 9th. At about 3:10 AM yesterday morning, the dormitory of the British Army Barracks in West Shanghai on Daxi Road suddenly caught fire accidentally. The Truth About the Meng Qingrong Wrongful Case of Accusation of Gambling Has Come to Light 159

Gamblers Conspire to Frame Him

Judge Corrects Wrongful Conviction

Meng Qingrong, a man from Shandong and awaiting assignment at the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, previously served in the bureau's Inspectorate at the direction of the bureau chief, specializing in cracking down on gambling. Because Meng was diligent in his work and had solved numerous lottery gambling cases, he was deeply resented by various lottery gambling ringleaders. Huang Yanxiaobao, a well-known lottery hooligan in the Nanshi area, had a particularly deep grudge against Meng. On December 1st of the previous year, at approximately 3:00 PM, he instigated his henchman, Zhang Yinbin (also known as Zhenyue), to open all the chests and trunks in his house, drag out and scatter all the clothes, making a complete mess. He then rushed out to report to the police officers on duty, claiming that Meng Qingrong, an official from the Police Bureau's Inspectorate who called himself Commissioner Meng, along with several companions wearing blue cloth short-sleeved shirts and trousers, had come to his house under the pretext of searching for lottery gambling activities, ransacked the chests and trunks, and conducted a thorough search, resulting in nothing being found. However, a gold bracelet, a gold ring, and a Wan Guochu Xu Hui savings certificate stored in the chest were allegedly stolen while they were there and taken away. He requested an investigation. Upon receiving the report, the police officers accompanied Zhang to his home at No. 1 Hengxing Dongli, 16th Pu, and found the chests open and the clothes scattered. They were unaware that this was Zhang's trickery and reported the situation to the district chief, who in turn reported it to the Municipal Police Bureau for review and handling. Upon hearing the report, Bureau Chief Wen sent officers to investigate. Because the matter involved dereliction of duty, Meng was immediately dismissed from his post and transferred to the court, where he was sentenced to five months' imprisonment. However, Meng argued that on December 1st of the previous year, he was under orders to go to the territory under the jurisdiction of the First District Second Precinct to arrest lottery gamblers. He had no free time to go to Zhang's house to conduct the search that Zhang accused him of. The imprisonment sentence was based on completely false facts. He refused to accept the sentence and immediately filed an appeal. After a detailed investigation by the court, it was finally revealed that Meng had indeed been falsely accused due to resentment. Therefore, the court announced the previous sentence overturned and declared him not guilty. The injustice Meng had suffered was finally redressed.

Anlegong Gambling Case Sentenced 160

Liu Heshang from Hangzhou, 25 years old, recently unemployed and bored, took advantage of the Lunar New Year holiday to open Room 10 on the third floor of the Anlegong Restaurant at No. 59 Sanyang Jingqiao, Aidoa Road, French Concession. He attracted gamblers to gamble on Pai Gow, poker, and mahjong, profiting from commissions. Every night, the gambling went on all night long, with huge wins and losses. The night before, the gambling was discovered by Xie Guangming and Hang Bingquan, the chief and deputy detectives of the French Concession Police's gambling squad. At 10:45 PM, they led Bao Tams He Zongyu, Cai Zongyi, Xu Chenghuai, and Xiao Yuping, along with Western detectives, to search the premises. Gamblers crowded the room, playing Pai Gow. Liu Heshang, the proprietor, and gamblers Yang Linsheng, Li Arong (an assistant in the pattern room of the British Public Works Department), Dai Liansheng, Wang Jintao, Liu Changsheng, Wu Jinsheng, and others, a total of twenty-two people, were arrested. Seized were one set of Pai Gow, one set of poker cards, one set of mahjong tiles, six dice, one shaker, gambling money of forty-seven yuan (including five counterfeit yuan), forty-six double-dime coins, and two hundred and fifty copper coins. Furthermore, because the Anlegong Restaurant allowed gambling, violating regulations, manager Chen Zhanxiong was also taken to the police station. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court, where Judge Zhang Chaozuo interrogated them. The police lawyer, Yao Zhaodi, explained the case and presented the gambling paraphernalia as evidence. Upon questioning, the defendants confessed to gathering to gamble and profiting from Pai Gow. Chen Zhanxiong also admitted to allowing guests to gamble. After reviewing the confessions, the court immediately sentenced Liu Heshang to one month's imprisonment and a fine of one hundred yuan. The gamblers were fined forty yuan, thirty yuan, twenty yuan, ten yuan, etc., respectively. Chen Zhanxiong was fined one hundred and sixty yuan for violating regulations. The gambling paraphernalia and money were confiscated. During the appeal period, the defendants were ordered to post bail and await further instructions.

The Case of Shooting a Prostitute Upheld the Original Verdict 161

Lin Rong, a chauffeur from Ningbo, was invited by his friend Chen Lanfang on the evening of January 4th of this year to a feast at the house of prostitute Lin Juxian in the Yaoertang brothel at No. 2 Hongyunfang, Route Wagner, French Concession. Chen, out of curiosity, took the live pistol of Zhou Hongsheng, a Bao Tam from the Public Concession who was also present. Accidentally pulling the trigger, the bullet shot out, fatally injuring the prostitute Lin Juxian. The police arrested Chen and brought him to the Second Special District Court for prosecution. The Higher Court had already opened a hearing, summoned witnesses, and reviewed the circumstances, as reported in previous newspapers. The case has now been finalized. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Chief Judge Guo, along with Judges Fan and Sun, announced in the Third Criminal Court that the appellant's appeal was rejected. During the appeal period of the third instance, the appellant remained on bail.

An Accomplice in a Robbery Four Years Ago Was Arrested 162

Xu Yongyuan, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, arrested Guo Ronghua (also known as Yao Xindi), a thief from Ningbo, in Donggui Lane, Huade Road, the day before yesterday. Investigation revealed that between December 28th, 1929, and January 5th, 1930, the defendant, along with Dai Rongxiang, Shen Aqing, and others who had already been convicted, used weapons to rob Xie Genyu at No. 246 Fengtian Road, Jin Defu at No. 557 Xinji Bang Road, Ni Lizhong at No. 558 on the same road, and Shen Wangshi at No. 352 Chongqing Road. Clothing and silver dollars worth over 1,500 yuan were stolen. The police chief ordered him to be detained. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Wang Yaotang, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, explained the past events, stating that the current defendants Dai and Shen could prove that they had robbed together at the time. Defendant Dai had confessed that the defendant was Yao Xindi, over thirty years old, with a scar on his face, which matched the description. The victims testified about the robbery, and the convicted defendants Dai Rongxiang, Shen Aqing, etc., all stated that the defendant Yao Xindi had indeed participated in the robbery. When questioned, the defendant's testimony was evasive. Judge Xiao Xiefen ordered him to be remanded in custody for further questioning.

The Central Bank - Issuance Reserve 189th Inspection Report states: According to Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, this council is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible banknotes. The 189th inspection was held at the Issuance Bureau of this bank on February 28th, 1934. The inspection results are announced as follows: (A) Total value of convertible banknotes issued: 71,298,922 silver dollars, including 64,967,052 silver dollar banknotes and 6,331,870 auxiliary currency banknotes. Total reserve fund for convertible banknotes: 71,298,922 silver dollars, including 58,228,922 silver dollars in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 54,791,881 yuan stored in the bank's issuance vault, 1,672,572 yuan stored in branches in various ports, and 1,764,469 yuan stored in other banks. The guaranteed reserve is equivalent to 13,070,000 silver dollars. (B) Total value of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes issued: 416,715.40 yuan. Total reserve fund for Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes: 416,715.40 yuan. This reserve includes 6,995.39 taels of standard gold, equivalent to 416,715.40 Customs Gold Units at a fixed price of 5957. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the guaranteed reserve is 40%. The inspection results show that the cash reserve exceeds 60% and the guaranteed reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This report is submitted. March 1, 1934, Li Fuxun, Chairman of the Supervisory Board of the Central Bank; Supervisors Xie Mingdong, Bei Songsun, Qin Runqing, Yu Qiaqing, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilao.

The Bank of Communications - Issuance Reserve Inspection Report states: The Bank of Communications' issuance of convertible banknotes and reserve funds for February 1934 have been inspected by supervisors Fu Qilin, He Shaoyin, and Xie Jishen, together with accountant Xu Yongzuo, on March 1st. The inspection results are listed as follows: Total value of convertible banknotes issued: 16,366,900 yuan. Meeting Minutes of the Nanhua Trade Association 166

The Nanhua Trade Association held a general meeting of members at Chongyi Hall the day before yesterday. The number of members present exceeded the legal quorum. Chairman Gong Jingyan performed the formalities, reporting the purpose of today's meeting: (1) Worshipping Guan Yu; (2) Members paying respect to each other; (3) Taking a photograph and having a wine gathering; and reading incoming and outgoing documents. The discussion then began: (1) Regarding the unsatisfactory performance of the Evaluation Committee in the past year, members believed that it should be rectified this year to avoid repeating the mistakes. Commissioner Gong proposed that all new members joining the association must pay a deposit of 100 yuan, collected from the tea certificate sales. Five members of the organization and custody committee will be established. Sanyang, Tianfu, Nancheng, and Datong will be responsible for the safekeeping and storage. Dasheng will be responsible for managing the passbook and receipts. In the future, if a member disrupts the price of goods, with conclusive evidence, the deposit will be confiscated in full, and penalties will be imposed, followed by handling according to industry regulations. If a member fails to pay the deposit, the sale of tea certificates will be suspended. Commissioner Xu seconded the motion, which was resolved and passed. (2) Regarding the proposed amendments to industry regulations, a clause was added to Article 6 of Chapter 3, stating that if a member opens a new store, the prices of similar goods from competitors within twenty storefronts on the left and right may follow the standard of the new store and may not exceed it. In Article 7 of Chapter 4, the market entry and exit permit for purchasing goods will be revoked on the third day. Those who are penalized on the first day of the same article will continue to be treated in the same way as a warning to others. (3) Discussion regarding the letter from the Vocational Union requesting various sections. It was resolved to collect 5 jiao per month from each member's clerk, collected by the association, and to notify members to comply. The meeting then adjourned.

The Inventor of the National Watermill Motor Visits the Mayor to Petition 171

The Result is Satisfactory: The Municipal Government Orders the Public Utilities Bureau to Verify and Report

Xu Peihuang Arranges for the Inventor to Have Detailed Discussions Today

Since the successful testing of the Watermill Motor (i.e., self-powered engine) invented by a Chinese citizen, Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao, the inventors, have submitted three petitions to the National Government and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting approval for assistance. Recently, the National Government approved and ordered the local competent authorities to verify and handle the matter. The inventors, Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao, went to the Municipal Government yesterday morning at 10:00 AM to visit Mayor Wu and petition him. The result was quite satisfactory, and Mayor Wu wrote a letter of introduction to Xu Peihuang, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, for detailed consultations on everything. The details are recorded as follows:

Petition Process 172

The inventors, Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao, went to the Municipal Government in the central district of the city at 10:00 AM yesterday morning, carrying a petition to visit Mayor Wu Tiecheng. Mayor Wu personally received them. Chen and Shan presented the petition and explained all the details, requesting Mayor Wu's assistance. Wu expressed deep encouragement and immediately ordered the First Section to write a letter of introduction to the Public Utilities Bureau for contact, verification, and reporting. In addition, Li Dachao, the head of the First Section, also wrote a letter of introduction to Xu Peihuang, Director of the Public Utilities Bureau, strongly supporting them. Chen and Shan, satisfied with the result, left at 11:30 AM and immediately went to the Public Utilities Bureau to visit Director Xu Peihuang. Xu sent Secretary Li to receive them and arranged for Director Xu to personally discuss everything at 2:00 PM this afternoon.

Petition to Mayor Wu 173

The original petition from the inventors to Mayor Wu reads: "Petition for assistance in the invention of a self-powered engine. Chunqiao, Xinbiao, and others have been researching for more than ten years, sacrificing countless efforts and finances, and have invented a 'self-powered engine' that does not require any fuel consumption, only a small amount of water, and can start the engine wheel with a twist of a knob. Its driving force is the same as that of existing motors and engines that use electricity, kerosene, and other fuels, and its advantages surpass them. The size of the horsepower can be constructed according to needs. After repeated tests, it has been successful. We originally intended to reproduce the entire machine and make it practical, but due to the excessive sacrifices made during the research, we have failed to fulfill our wishes. Therefore, we respectfully submitted a petition to the National Government, requesting assistance, and submitted a petition to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting approval for protection, etc. We recently received a reply from the Chairman of the National Government, stating, 'If there is indeed an invention, drawings and instructions should be submitted to the Academia Sinica or the local competent authorities for verification and handling.' In response, we have attached drawings and instructions to this petition and personally visit Your Excellency to present the details in person. If this is not the case, how dare we come here boldly? We earnestly implore Your Excellency to approve our request and provide guidance. Respectfully presented to Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai Municipality, by petitioners Chen Xinbiao and Shan Chunqiao."

Order to the Public Utilities Bureau 174

The First Section of the Municipal Government, according to Mayor Wu's instructions, wrote a letter of introduction to the Public Utilities Bureau for contact on everything. The original letter reads: "Respectfully, we recently received a piece from Shan Chunqiao and Chen Xinbiao, submitted by Mayor Wu, regarding a request for assistance in the invention of a self-powered engine, and a letter of instructions to contact the Public Utilities Bureau, verify, and handle the matter, and report. Accordingly, we are copying the original letter and sending it to you, hoping that you will verify, contact, handle the matter, and reply. Respectfully to the Public Utilities Bureau, from the First Section of the Municipal Government." In addition, Li Dachao, the head of the section, also wrote a letter of introduction to Xu Peihuang, Director of the Bureau. The original letter reads: "Brother Juntao, Greetings. Chen Xinbiao, the inventor of the self-powered engine, has come to the government to visit the Mayor. We have received instructions to introduce him to your bureau for review. Please order the department to investigate in detail and provide as much support as possible. I am introducing Mr. Chen to you. I hope you will grant him an audience. With best wishes, Li Dachao."
