Construction of Long-Distance Telephone Line on the Shanghai-Nanjing Highway Begins 176

The Total Length of the Line is 232 Miles

The Total Cost is 500,000 Yuan

It is Expected that Calls Can Be Made in April

Regarding the construction of a long-distance telephone line on the Shanghai-Nanjing Highway, the National Economic Council previously stated that the highway was of great importance to the transportation between the capital and Shanghai. Before its completion, a telephone line should be constructed first to meet the needs of road construction. It had consulted with the Ministry of Communications to actively carry out the construction. A reporter from Xin Xin News learned from the Ministry of Communications that the construction of the telephone line had already begun after the Ministry of Communications had made appropriate plans. The long-distance telephone line runs from Nanjing, through Jurong, Yixing, Wuxi, Changshu, and Taicang, to Shanghai, with a total length of 232 miles. 6,715 wooden poles have been purchased, and four pairs of No. 10 steel wires will be installed. In addition to using ordinary intersections, it is also planned to install phantom intersections. After the entire line is completed, there will be six electrical circuits. All construction work is currently underway in sections. It is estimated that the entire line will be open for calls in three or four months. The total cost is 500,000 yuan.

Citizens Must Get Vaccinated Against Smallpox 177

Children and Adults Should Get Vaccinated Every Three Years for Best Results

Because the Effectiveness of Vaccination Gradually Decreases Over Time

According to the Director of the Public Health Department of the Public Works Department, people generally believe that once vaccinated against smallpox, they are immune for life. This view has now been proven to be inaccurate. According to statistics and observations in the United States and elsewhere, the effectiveness of vaccination gradually decreases over time. Therefore, it is now generally recognized that children who have been vaccinated at a very young age must be revaccinated at the age of seven. After the age of seven, adults should be revaccinated every three years to strengthen their

Protection Against Smallpox 178

However, people often forget the danger when they are safe. Once smallpox has been eliminated, people hesitate to get vaccinated. When prevention is neglected, smallpox inevitably becomes prevalent again, and then people rush to get vaccinated. Looking at the figures for the previous year in this district, smallpox was initially rare, but it suddenly became prevalent in December and January, and the number of vaccinations also increased sharply. Vaccination is the most effective way to prevent smallpox. Looking at the statistics from the previous year, the Chinese Isolation Hospital under the Bureau received a total of 137 patients with smallpox throughout the year, of which 49 died. Among the deceased, 34 had never been vaccinated at all, and the remaining 12 had been vaccinated, but it was more than three years ago. Out of the total of 137 patients admitted, 50 had never been vaccinated, and 77 had not been revaccinated on schedule. Therefore, the

Importance of Vaccination 179

Cannot be overemphasized. Moreover, smallpox can occur under any circumstances, regardless of wealth or poverty, and regardless of the poor or good living conditions. Therefore, it is hoped that all people, for their own sake and for the sake of the public, will implement the "vaccinate once every three years" method to avoid the spread of smallpox.

Big Fire in Zhabei Wasteland 180

More Than Fifty Thatched and Tile Houses Were Destroyed

The Arsonist is on the Run; Only a Suspect Has Been Arrested

Behind Xiangyuan Lane on Zhangqiao Road in Zhabei was originally a wasteland, covering more than thirty mu. Ten years ago, it was occupied by poor people from Jiangbei, who built thatched houses. To date, there are more than three hundred houses, lined up side by side, forming a market town. However, the fuel used by the poor is all straw, so fires often occur due to forgotten embers, causing fires. In the winter of the previous year, it was once completely burned down, causing an unprecedented tragedy. Unexpectedly, at around 3:30 AM yesterday morning, a fire suddenly broke out at the home of Chen Wentao, who works as a driver for the Public Concession Tram Company. Chen had returned home after finishing work at midnight and was hungry, so he cooked porridge to eat. Accidentally, a spark fell on the straw, and by the time he noticed it, the fire had become a prairie fire. Moreover, due to the dry weather, it spread easily. A group of neighbors were awakened from their dreams and fled in panic. At the same time, although this place is under the jurisdiction of the Third Precinct of the Fifth District, there is no station set up, so by the time the residents ran to the precinct to report, the fire was out of control. The Zhabei fire brigades received the news and quickly sent fire engines to the scene to put out the fire. However, there were no firefighting facilities here, so the firefighters could not help. Therefore, the fire spread further, reaching Baolingtang Pharmacy at No. 110 Zhangqiao Road and the buildings at Nos. 7 and 8 Xiangyuan Lane. Fortunately, the nearby waterways were pointed out by the residents, and the firefighters quickly extended the hoses to the Shajing River and drew water to put out the fire. After about two hours, the entire fire was extinguished. As a result, more than forty thatched houses and ten tile houses were destroyed, as well as two buildings in Xiangyuan Lane and two rear buildings and attics of Baolingtang. The losses were significant. The arsonist, Chen Wentao, fled without a trace after the fire broke out. Only a suspect, Li Jinxiu, was arrested. After being interrogated by the Third Precinct of the Fifth District, he was released on bail. Meanwhile, the arsonist is being pursued for interrogation.

Rakehell's Relentless Pursuit Drives Young Woman to Jump from Building in Desperation 181

A Gold Ring Sparks Endless Disputes

Four Front Teeth Barely Escape Death

Dong Luyuan, a young man of 19, residing at No. 74, Miezhu Street, outside the Great East Gate in the South City, lost his parents and inherited real estate worth over ten thousand yuan. Unmarried, he previously studied at school, but recently dropped out to indulge in a life of idleness and neglecting his proper occupation. Qian Yangshi, a woman from Huzhou, aged 41, living in the front building of the three-story house above the octagonal shop (i.e., the overpass building in De Xing Lane), No. 585, Fada Road, had a deceased husband and a daughter named A'bao, aged 19. A'bao possessed a somewhat ordinary appearance. About a month ago, she encountered Dong on the road. Because Dong's face was covered with pockmarks, he was immediately struck by A'bao's beauty, considering her a celestial being. However, he did not know her residence and had no way to communicate his affections. Fortunately, Dong had a friend nicknamed Zhang Jiuguan, who was acquainted with a Mr. Lu living in the back building of A'bao's residence. Zhang, knowing Dong's intentions, led him to Lu's place. From then on, Dong was able to see A'bao more often, gradually striking up conversations and getting closer. Later, Dong visited A'bao's house every afternoon, using playing mahjong as a pretext to seduce her. A'bao, being young and with her affections newly awakened, disregarded the consequences and was eventually enticed by Dong. Dong, feeling that the time was ripe, on the evening of the fifteenth day of the twelfth lunar month of the previous year, lured A'bao out under the pretense of watching a movie. They went to a hotel together and engaged in intimate relations. Afterward, A'bao asked Dong for a coat, but Dong was stingy and only gave her his own nine-carat gold ring as a memento. Since then, their affections were intertwined. However, beautiful scenes do not last. Recently, Dong found out that A'bao had another lover, and he felt extremely resentful. On the afternoon of the seventeenth of last month (i.e., the third day of the Lunar New Year), at about nine o'clock, he first went to A'bao's house alone to borrow two yuan, in an attempt to test her feelings. At that time, A'bao replied that money matters were handled by her mother and she could not comply with his request. At this point, Dong, feeling that he was being treated coldly and denied the loan, was certain that A'bao had another lover. He left in a fit of anger. Later, he gathered four hooligans, including Gao Fusheng and Zhang Jiuguan, and rushed to A'bao's house to argue with her. They forcibly removed the gold ring she was wearing on her hand. In addition, one of the hooligans with bad eyes slapped A'bao twice on the cheek. A'bao, unable to bear the humiliation, felt overwhelmed with shame and resentment. Taking advantage of a moment when no one was paying attention, she opened the window and jumped onto the balcony, throwing herself down onto Fada Road. When Dong and the others saw A'bao falling, they scattered and fled the building, disappearing without a trace. A'bao, due to the high fall, lost four front teeth, broke her right leg, and fainted from the pain. Her mother, Qian Yangshi, rushed down, hired a car, and sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. Meanwhile, A'bao's mother, believing that her daughter's suicide attempt was caused by Dong's coercion, reported the incident to the Dazimingzhong Police Station, requesting an arrest and investigation. The police chief, upon receiving the report, immediately dispatched Detective Lu Dongliang, No. 97, to investigate and inquire about Dong's whereabouts. By three o'clock the next afternoon, they learned that Dong was hiding at a friend's place on the upper floor of a tin shop at No. 343, West Zilaihuo Street. They secretly went to the address, arrested Dong, confiscated the gold ring, and took him to the police station to be sent to the Second District Local Court for interrogation and investigation. Yesterday, Judge Qiu Huanying continued the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. Yao Zhaodi, the police station's lawyer, explained the police station's investigation process, accusing Dong of robbery in collusion with three or more people, according to Article 348 of the Criminal Law. Subsequently, Dong testified that the gold ring was a gift he gave to A'bao. He bought the gold ring three months ago at Lao Qingyun Silver Shop with his niece-in-law, spending ten yuan. This time, when he asked A'bao for money, she took off the gold ring and threw it on the table because she didn't have any money. He did not rob her by force, nor did he beat her. He hired a lawyer to defend him and requested bail. The police station's lawyer opposed bail, arguing that Dong's crime was very serious. They then questioned the plaintiff, Qian Yangshi, about Dong's robbery of the gold ring and A'bao's jumping from the building. After verifying the testimonies in court, the judge ordered a postponement until the morning of the seventh for further questioning. The defendant provided a reliable shop as guarantor and assumed a guarantee responsibility of 5,000 yuan, otherwise he would be detained without bail.

Cohabitation Begins After Mahjong Gatherings 182

Cohabitation Ends After a Year with a Divorce

Accusations of Abandonment and Fraud

Shi Wenying, a woman from Suzhou, residing at No. 5, Gufuli, Dagu Road, is thirty-two years old and does not have a formal spouse. She lives with her elderly mother, who earns a living by spinning yarn, while she supports herself by washing clothes for others. Wu Hongzhang, a man from Ningbo, nearly fifty years old, residing at No. 23, Fushouli, Airjin Road, was introduced to Shi's house to play mahjong in the summer of the year before last. He became acquainted with Wenying. Although Wenying is a middle-aged woman and not particularly beautiful, Wu was fond of her and said that his wife's position was still vacant, willing to make a lifelong commitment. Thus, they began to live together as husband and wife. Wu was responsible for the household expenses, providing thirty yuan a month. However, after only a year, Wu suddenly stopped coming, neglecting Shi and her mother. Although they repeatedly reasoned with him, there was no satisfactory outcome. Wenying then filed a criminal complaint with the First Special District Local Court against Wu for abandonment and fraud. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Huang Risheng opened the court to summon the parties for questioning. The plaintiff, Shi Wenying, testified that after she began cohabiting with the defendant in September of the year before last, the defendant suddenly told her one day that he needed money and asked her to find a way to get him 1,000 yuan. She, thinking that they were husband and wife, could not refuse and borrowed 400 yuan from a close female friend, along with 200 yuan from her mother's savings for her coffin, and gave it all to the defendant. However, after obtaining the money, he disappeared and never came back. She later learned that the defendant already had a wife and that his previous words were all lies. Therefore, she is now accusing him of abandonment and fraud. When questioned, the defendant, Wu Hongzhang, admitted to going to the plaintiff's house to gamble and knowing the plaintiff, but firmly denied defrauding the plaintiff of money. However, Shi Wenying claimed that she could invite the friend who lent her the money to testify in court. Judge Huang then ordered a postponement for further questioning.

Female Principal Accuses Female Teacher's Father-in-Law 183

Leading a Large Group of Students to Observe the Trial

Conflicting Testimonies, Awaiting Further Investigation

Zhuo Jiezhen, the female principal of Baocui Primary School in Tianfuli, Airjin Road, previously hired a lawyer to file a case in the First Special District Court against Zhong Yaorong, the owner of the Hao Shi Lai Food Shop on Jielu Road, accusing him of obstructing freedom and defaming her reputation. The Special Court has already summoned the parties for questioning once, but the defendant did not appear, and the hearing was postponed. Details have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Liu Yugui took the bench in the Second Criminal Court to continue the hearing. The plaintiff, Zhuo Jiezhen, led the entire student body of the school, about seventy or eighty boys and girls, to the court to observe the trial. The defendant, Zhong Yaorong, also came to court with his attorney, Wu Shaoshan. The plaintiff, Zhuo Jiezhen, stated that she founded Baocui Primary School in 1928. On January 13 of this year, she hired Ms. Zhong Quyue'e as a teacher. Ms. Zhong is the defendant's daughter-in-law and the daughter of the introducer, Qu Yuehua. Before teaching for even half a month, Quyue'e suddenly took two days of leave on January 29 and 30, and did not return to school after the expiration of her leave, resulting in the suspension of classes. Because the school's reputation and the children's studies were affected, she and her husband, Tan Qingpu, went to the defendant's place on February 1 with Quyue'e's younger sister, Qu Yuechan, to negotiate. The defendant then accused her of impersonating the principal and abducting his daughter-in-law. He also incited the shop staff to beat her and her husband, restricting their freedom. After two hours, he called the police to send them to the police station, and they were later released. However, the defendant's insulting remarks and restriction of freedom constitute defamation and obstruction of freedom. When questioned, the defendant, Zhong Yaorong, stated that Qu Yue'e is his daughter-in-law, but he did not know that she was teaching at the plaintiff's school. On February 1, the plaintiff and her husband came to make a scene, saying that his daughter-in-law owed them money. However, because his daughter-in-law had been involved in litigation with him for years, he did not know her whereabouts, so he refused them. He did not expect the plaintiff to gather many people and come to beat him, so he called the police together to the police station. He did not accuse her of impersonating the principal or abducting his daughter-in-law. The witness, Qu Yuechan, testified that the defendant restricted Principal Zhuo's freedom and insulted her. Judge Liu stated that further investigation of this case was necessary and ordered a postponement to the sixth for further questioning.

Dongjiadu Ferry Service Operated by the Municipal Government to Be Realized 184

Service Can Start in the Summer of This Year

The Dongjiadu Ferry Terminal in this city is a major route for people traveling to and from the three counties of Shangnan Chuan. More than 10,000 citizens cross the Huangpu River every day, making it the most important ferry terminal. The Municipal Government, recognizing the needs of the citizens, had planned to prepare a municipal service as early as 1928, but the project required a large amount of funding, so it was delayed. Recently, the Fifth District Executive Committee of the Municipal Party Department, recognizing the dangerous overloading of passengers on the existing ferry services and for the purpose of revitalizing the Pudong commercial market, submitted a request to the Municipal Party Department's Executive Committee, requesting the Municipal Government to quickly take back the municipal operation and open a ferry service to facilitate public travel. The Executive Committee's three standing committee members, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, and Tong Xingbai, sent a letter to the Municipal Government, urging it to instruct the Xingye Trust Company to organize the ferry service. The Municipal Government has replied that the Dongjiadu cross-river ferry is currently being actively prepared by the Xingye Trust Company. The Municipal Government also received requests from all sectors of industry, commerce, and education in Tangqiao Township, Pudong, requesting the speedy establishment of the Dongjiadu ferry service, and therefore urged the Xingye Trust Company to actively prepare for it. It is now learned that the company has raised more than 100,000 yuan in capital for the Dongjiadu ferry service plan and is planning detailed designs for the ferry and wharf. It is said that the future Dongjiadu cross-river ferry's wharf and ferry equipment will be superior to the existing equipment on Dongmen Road. Specially made double-ended copper-hulled ferries will be used, which will be stable to sail and easy to berth. Therefore, the crossing time will only take a maximum of two minutes each time. Once the design plan is completed, a public tender will be held, and it is expected that the service can be implemented in the summer of this year.

Request for Exemption from Tax on Low-Quality Diesel Fuel 185

A Document Presented by the Zhejiang Private Electricity Industry Association to the Legislative Yuan

The Zhejiang Private Electricity Industry Association, located at No. 212 Nanjing Road in this city, stated that the tax increase on low-quality diesel fuel has a significant impact on the electricity industry. It has already petitioned the Legislative Yuan to find a way to provide relief. The original document is as follows: The petition is about the extremely heavy tax on diesel fuel, which could lead to the demise of the electricity industry. It is hoped that the Legislative Yuan will quickly provide relief to alleviate the difficulties of businesses and save them from their predicament. It is reported that Announcement No. 1335, jointly issued by the Jianghai Customs Superintendent and the Commissioner of Customs, states that in accordance with the order of the Ministry of Finance, new standards for taxing imported diesel fuel have been established: (A) Thick diesel fuel: 2.90 yuan gold units per ton; (B) Thin diesel fuel (including crude oil for refining): 26.30 yuan gold units per ton, approximately equivalent to 49 yuan in national currency, effective from February 1, 1934. Upon hearing this, the members of the association were panicked and believed that the current price of thin diesel fuel is more than 70 yuan per ton, and the increased tariff has reached 70% of the fuel price. Business operations will be impossible to maintain and will be in a dire situation. They have repeatedly appealed to the government to find a way to provide relief. The Zhejiang Provincial Electricity Company uses diesel engines for power generation, accounting for 89% (the situation in other provinces is similar). The annual demand for diesel fuel is more than 6,000 tons. According to the current fuel price calculation, the loss will reach more than 300,000 yuan. Adding the losses of other provinces, the number is even more alarming. At a time when all industries are declining and rural areas are bankrupt, the electricity industry has been greatly affected. However, because it concerns public use and is closely related to factory production and social security, it can only be maintained with great pain, even if income cannot cover expenses. In Article 33 of Chapter 4 of the Provisional Constitution of the Republic of China during the Political Tutelage Period, promulgated by the National Government on June 1, 1931, it is stated that in order to develop the people's livelihood, the state should provide encouragement and protection for the people's production enterprises. The telegram jointly issued by Chairman Jiang and President Wang also regards production and construction as the main task of saving the nation and seeking survival and calls on the people of the country to work together. It can be seen that they have a far-sighted view and are deeply concerned about the people's suffering. We are deeply grateful and grateful. Electric lights and electric heat are necessary for people's daily use, and electricity is necessary for various small industries and farmland irrigation. It can be seen that the electricity industry is completely used in the people's production enterprises. The Executive Yuan also issued an order in June 1930 to reduce and exempt exorbitant taxes and fees and support the development of the electricity industry. Now, the Ministry of Finance has suddenly increased the diesel fuel tax rate, making it impossible for power plants and people to bear the burden, and they will inevitably fall into a desperate situation. This is close to destroying industry and violating the Provisional Constitution, and we should ask for correction. According to the current tariff standards, from No. 244 to No. 254, all kinds of machines used in agriculture, industry, and commerce are taxed ad valorem when imported from foreign countries, and the regulations are from 5% to 7.5%. The original intention was that China's industry is still in its infancy, and machinery is a tool for encouraging production and developing industry. The aim is to reduce costs and promote it widely. The reduction of machinery tax is of profound significance, and diesel fuel is the fuel for driving machinery. Therefore, the tariffs previously levied were also similar to machinery tax. Now, the Ministry of Finance suddenly taxes thin diesel fuel at 70% of the ad valorem value. The previous and the latter contradict each other, which violates the tariff standards. Ignoring the difficulties of businesses and going against the trend is not acceptable to merchants. We should ask for correction. We found that the Legislative Yuan held its 46th meeting of the third session on February 9 of this year. Item 6 of the discussion items: The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan suggested that the Legislative Yuan should consult with the Executive Yuan and issue an order to all provinces and cities to report all existing taxes and fees' names, methods, tax rates, tax revenue, start date, and reasons for collection to the Ministry of Finance before the end of June of this year, and then the Executive Yuan will transfer them to the Legislative Yuan for review. The resolution was: Pass the proposed opinions. Item 7: The Finance Committee of the Legislative Yuan suggested that the Legislative Yuan should ask the National Government to issue an order to all central government agencies, and all taxes and fees collected and contracts concluded that have undergone legislative procedures should be submitted to the Legislative Yuan for resolution before the end of April of this year to emphasize the spirit of the rule of law and conform to the government's orders. The resolution was: Pass the proposed opinions. Therefore, if the Ministry of Finance's heavy increase in the diesel fuel tax rate this time has not been reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan, it cannot be implemented according to law. We should ask for correction. Diesel fuel is a necessity for power plants, other small industries, and shipping. China currently has no mining and must rely on imports. Thick diesel fuel has too many impurities, which can easily damage machinery, and there is no stock on the market. Therefore, all power plants use thin diesel fuel to ensure the safety of machinery. It is heard that a small number of domestic merchants refine kerosene from this thin diesel fuel to profit from it, which hinders tax revenue. Therefore, a heavy tax is levied on thin diesel fuel to provide an invisible resistance. If this is the case, then to deal with the small number of oil refining merchants, it is advisable to formulate better methods and order local governments to strictly crack down, which is not difficult to clean up within the time limit. In this way, the government can still protect its original tax revenue. Otherwise, if the two are not distinguished, and the meal is abandoned due to choking, our legitimate power plants will be innocently harmed and fall into a hopeless situation, which is close to a suicidal policy. It is reported that the Shanghai shipping industry and the machine water lifting industry in the counties along the Jinghu Railway have successively appealed to withdraw the order. It is enough to prove that the implementation of this case is related to the rise and fall of agriculture, industry, and commerce throughout the country, especially the life and death of our electricity industry. We especially ask the Legislative Yuan to review and approve. It is hoped that the Legislative Yuan will take into account the difficulties of businesses and allow them to consult with the Executive Yuan to transfer to the Ministry of Finance to quickly tax the relevant thin diesel fuel tariffs at the same rate as thick diesel fuel to show fairness and protect the electricity industry. We are waiting for instructions and will comply. This is for public convenience. Respectfully presented to the President of the Legislative Yuan, Sun, Chairman of the Zhejiang Private Electricity Industry Association, Li Yanshi.

Since Lin took office, he has personally studied and carefully handled the appraisal cases submitted by the court, because they are all related to the parties' debt responsibilities or criminal charges, and the entry and exit are extremely important. He has upheld the principles of justice, but unexpectedly there have been false accusations. Fortunately, the court was fair and acquitted him. C. Members Gao Huai, Gong Zhaoqiu, etc. sent a letter requesting temporary withdrawal from the association. Reading Q&A: A Further Discussion on Learning Language 194

Since the last time I published an article "On Learning Language" (see this column on February 6, 7, and 8), many readers have written to question this issue. For example, Mr. Huang Lixiong asked:

(1) Is "prosody and timbre" only found in classical Chinese? Is it worth the effort for people who study new literature?

(2) How to appreciate "divine principle and flavor" and "masculine and feminine"?

(3) What are the benefits of studying classical Chinese?

(4) Is the current language consistent in speech and writing?

(5) Sometimes when I read other people's articles, I often encounter many adjectives or nouns, and I can't grasp their meaning, such as the words "divine principle and flavor" and "prosody and timbre." What is the remedy?

Mr. Tan Mengruo asked:

(1) Regarding national literature, according to you, modern people should study modern Chinese, but it is said that as a citizen of a country, one should understand or be able to read all historical records. The writings left by the ancients to later generations are like a concrete machine, which needs to be modified and integrated by later generations to form an independent style. Another saying is that the philosophers and scholars of the pre-Qin period are the seasonings, and the Twenty-Four Histories are the raw materials. Today, all new literature writers have read ancient books. So, is it necessary to read classical Chinese only to become an expert? If one only seeks to obtain and use ordinary writing, should one not bother to read classical Chinese, so as not to go around in circles?

The above questions can be summarized into three types: (1) Why shouldn't one start with classical Chinese when reading Chinese? (2) How to explain "prosody and timbre" and "divine principle and flavor"? (3) Is speech and writing consistent? The following are the answers:

(1) Why shouldn't one start with classical Chinese when reading Chinese?

This question has already been discussed last time, and I didn't want to say it again, but the general readers are still infatuated with classical Chinese, so I should simply state our reasons again.

First, we know that language is a medium for conveying thought. As long as the thought is explained, the tool for expressing the thought can be ignored. However, if there is a major change in thought and a major change in social organization, then the language, the medium for conveying thought, must also be changed. Because the old form cannot express the new thought at this time. Now our Chinese thought has undergone a major change under the influence of Europe and the United States, so there is the so-called "literary revolution," the reason for which is that the simple form and composition of the language cannot convey new thoughts. This is a fact, and it is also commonly felt by those who translate scientific books now. The translation of *The Wealth of Nations* by Yan Ji, which we mentioned last time, cannot express the original meaning clearly, is a very obvious example.

Second, from the perspective of the "words" used, we know that language is constantly undergoing the process of metabolism. On the one hand, it is creating new words and adding combined words; on the other hand, it is also eliminating old words. The reason is the same as mentioned above, that is, as human knowledge increases day by day, language must also expand accordingly, so the old words are felt to be insufficient and cannot be used as symbols of new concepts. On the other hand, many old concepts of the old era no longer exist in later generations, so those "words" that represent old concepts are gradually forgotten and gradually eliminated because they are not suitable. (Regarding this, readers can refer to Chen Wangdao's *An Outline of Rhetoric*, page 67, and Lu Simian's *Brief Explanation of Characters*, chapters on the reproduction and elimination of characters)

Third, the above two reasons are about the changes in language, and this is still the reason why we want to use modern Chinese. In other words, if readers read Chinese for practical purposes, they must read modern Chinese. What we want to point out now is, should learning modern Chinese start with classical Chinese? This is what readers are most doubtful about and urgently need an answer to. Why shouldn't readers start with classical Chinese when reading modern Chinese? The reason is this: Our language has undergone major changes in style, syntax, and word usage. It is very different from classical Chinese. Of course, the characters are still passed down from ancient times. Mr. Tan's letter compares classical Chinese to a machine, which is acceptable, but his explanation is wrong. If classical Chinese is an old machine, then modern Chinese is a new machine that has been greatly improved based on the old machine. True, the new machine is the successor of the old machine, the evolution of the old machine. However, people who learn to use machines do not necessarily need to start with learning to use old machines. Although the methods of using new machines are the same as those of old machines in some places, most of them are different. Therefore, people who know how to use old machines must also learn anew if they want to use new machines. Of course, his learning will be easier than those who have not learned to use machines, but this is not enough to be a lesson, because for those who do not know how to use either new or old machines, why bother to spend two steps to learn two methods of use? In order to use the new machine, he should directly learn the method of using the new machine. Many of the old machine usage methods are not needed on the new machine. What's the use of learning them? The reason why we advise people to learn Chinese from modern Chinese is this. (To be continued)

Comments on Raising Silver Prices and China's Purchasing Power by Mu Jiaji 195

The idea of the United States raising silver prices to increase the purchasing power of the Far East is something I have heard a lot about in recent years. Recently, this kind of noise has become louder and louder, with a great tendency to be implemented immediately. As for whether the implementation of raising silver prices can really increase the purchasing power of the Far East, how the Far East will be affected, and what defensive methods there will be, answering these kinds of questions is the mission of this article. First of all, two points need to be explained: (1) The so-called increasing the purchasing power of the Far East actually refers only to China, because India abandoned the silver standard in 1893, using silver internally and gold externally, so the level of silver prices does not have much impact on India. (2) The so-called raising of silver prices refers to the separate price of silver, and not to raising it at the same time as other prices. If silver prices and general prices are raised at the same time, it will not be very harmful to our country. For example, in the past few years, prices and silver prices fell at the same time, so the theoretical advantages and disadvantages are different from the facts. (See my book "Monetary Issues in China's Foreign Economy in the Last Four Years," published in the Central Bank Monthly Report, December 1933) In the years before this world economic panic, the economies of various countries were prosperous to the extreme. This phenomenon was most evident in the United States. At that time, there was a very popular name called "New Era," which meant that the economic situation at that time had reached a new era. From then on, they could only go on the golden road and would never return to the pain of pre-war economic cycles. Who knew that in 1929, New York stock prices fell sharply, and since then, all prices have fallen. Some people could not find the real cause of the panic and were at a loss. Some people thought that this phenomenon was only temporary and would not have a great impact. At the same time, some people took the opportunity to advocate that the reason for the decline in prices was mainly due to the fall in silver prices (in fact, since India implemented the sale of silver reserves in 1927, silver prices fell to the end of 1929 and then plummeted along with general prices). For example, Thomas W. Lamont, a famous New York banker, said in early 1930, "The main reason for the world economic panic is the lack of gold and the fall in silver prices." President Hoover said in his speech at the Cleveland Bank Association on October 2, 1930, analyzing the causes of the panic, "The purchasing power of China and India is determined by silver prices, and it has been greatly hit." This kind of argument was common in the first two years of the panic, but later, after considerable research on the causes of the panic, except for the silver faction and those related to Far Eastern business, this kind of argument gradually disappeared. Now, according to the facts, examining whether the fall in silver prices is a major cause of the economic panic, we can say in reverse whether raising silver prices is a countermeasure to save the panic. The following is a list of the percentage increase or decrease in the value of imports and exports of major countries in 1930 and 1931.

(1) Imports

Compared to 1929 Compared to 1930

1930 Increase (+) or Decrease (-) 1931 Increase (+) or Decrease (-)

(1) (1)

A. Calculated in silver (+) 3.6% (+) 4.4%

China

B. Calculated in gold (-) 27.0% (-) 20.0%

United States (-) 28.1% (-) 33.1%

United Kingdom (-) 13.9% (-) 16.7%

Japan (-) 30.5% (-) 19.9%

France (-) 9.8% (-) 19.6%

(2) Exports

Compared to 1929 Compared to 1930

1930 Increase (+) or Decrease (-) 1931 Increase (+) or Decrease (-)

(1) (1)

A. Calculated in silver (-) 11.8% (+) 1.6%

China

B. Calculated in gold (-) 34.0% (-) 25.0%

United States (-) 21.9% (-) 41.0%

United Kingdom (-) 21.8% (-) 31.8%

Japan (-) 31.9% (-) 21.8%

France (-) 14.7% (-) 28.9%

Looking at the above table, the value of our country's imported goods, calculated in silver, only increased and did not decrease. As for the value calculated in gold, it decreased by 27% in 1930 compared to 1929, and by 20% in 1931 compared to 1930. However, the imported goods of the United States and Japan also had the same decrease. There is another level that must be paid attention to, that is, although our country's population accounts for more than one-fifth of the world's population, the amount of foreign trade is often around 2.5% of the total value of world international trade. Therefore, our country's imports in 1930, calculated in gold, decreased by 27%, which actually only decreased by less than 1% in the entire world international trade (that is, 27% multiplied by 2.5%). The extent to which a decrease of less than 1% in the total world international trade will affect the world economic panic can be imagined. As for exports, the value of our country calculated in gold has shrunk almost more than any country in the table, which is inconsistent with the theoretical saying that the fall in silver prices can encourage exports. In fact, because our country is a country with insufficient production, and the prices of agricultural products have plummeted, and the overseas recession is the reason, exports have decreased a lot. From the above situation, it seems undoubtedly that the decline in silver prices is not a cause of this world economic panic. However, there are still silver factions and those related to Eastern business who are still singing the song of raising silver prices to increase the purchasing power of the Far East. Not only are they singing loudly, but they also have considerable power in the United States and may force the government to implement it. The following will try to describe what impact it will have on China after the silver price is actually raised. However, this matter is of great importance, and what is described is only a general overview. Before describing it, first clarify the two words "silver price." Before countries abandoned the gold standard, the so-called silver price referred to the value of silver calculated in gold, and our country's foreign exchange rate also fluctuated up and down within a considerable range with this price. After countries abandoned the gold standard, the so-called silver price refers to the value of silver calculated in paper currency. For example, the London silver price after the United Kingdom abandoned the gold standard on September 21, 1931, refers to the value of silver calculated in paper pounds, and our country's exchange rate against the British pound also fluctuated up and down within a considerable range with this price. After other countries abandoned the gold standard, the same can be inferred. We must know that since countries abandoned the gold standard, the silver price (that is, the price of silver calculated in paper pounds or paper dollars) and our country's foreign exchange rate have already increased a lot, especially in the past year. In other words, after countries abandoned the gold standard, the foreign value of their paper currency naturally fell, and the result was that our country's currency value was diligently raised. This situation has been going on for one or two years. Understanding the impact that our country has suffered in the past one or two years, we can infer the impact after the silver price is raised again. The most noteworthy point is that our country is a silver-using country, not a silver-producing country, so since 1910, except for the period of the European War, it has imported a large amount of silver every year. However, last year was like the situation during the European War, when the foreign silver price was higher than the domestic silver price, and our country actually became an exporter of silver, with a value of about 50 million yuan. We still remember that in 1930 and 1931, the foreign silver price plummeted, causing the domestic silver price to be higher than the foreign silver price, and a large amount of cash silver flowed into our country. This phenomenon (that is, an object runs from a market with a low price to a market with a high price), if not stopped, can flow out like water going downhill. In the past one or two years, silver has been exported a lot due to the attraction of high prices abroad. If the silver price is raised again, the export of silver will inevitably be greater than last year. The impact of a non-silver-producing silver-using country exporting a large amount of cash silver on the national economy is naturally very great and can be self-evident. After the silver price is raised, in addition to the export of silver, the impact on our country's import and export goods will also be significant. Now countries are suffering from overproduction, while our country is suffering from insufficient production. After the silver price is raised, the surplus goods of foreign countries will again use our country as the tail, and a large number of them will be imported. According to the facts in the past one or two years, it can be proved that, according to the author's observation, our country's economic panic did not start in 1929, but at the end of 1931 when countries abandoned the gold standard. Of course, after 1931, our country's economy was greatly hit by the September 18th Incident and the January 28th Incident, but the dumping of foreign goods, which was unheard of before 1931 and has been reported in newspapers every day since then, is also a major reason (most of which is currency dumping). If the silver price is raised again, the wave of bankruptcies of our country's industrial and commercial enterprises may be even worse than today. There will also be extremely unfavorable effects on exports, because our country's overseas markets have been taken away by others. After the silver price is raised again, the value of our country's exports calculated in gold must also be raised. Therefore, the sales of our country's export commodities abroad will be further reduced. The result of raising the silver price is like this. The so-called increase in the purchasing power of the Far East is not only impossible, but it will also cause greater damage to our country's economy, and the purchasing power will inevitably be further reduced. So, how can purchasing power be increased? Only by increasing production, because currency is only a medium of exchange. If there are more outputs, there must also be more inputs to balance it. This is the case for both individuals and countries. It is not possible to supplement the purchasing power of a country by raising or lowering the value of a country's currency. Therefore, the production conference that is about to be held is shouldering a major mission. The impact of raising silver prices on our country has been described above. For the sake of self-defense, our country has to take decisive measures. First, we should impose heavy taxes on or even prohibit the import of imported goods that are harmful to or unnecessary for our country's inherent or future industrial and commercial enterprises, so as to avoid the bankruptcy of domestic industrial and commercial enterprises. We must recognize that this kind of currency dumping tax does not increase the burden on consumers, but aims to maintain the balance of domestic prices. Second, banning silver exports within a considerable period of time is also an inevitable step to prevent the outflow of cash silver. Finally, judging from the current situation, there should be a permanent organization to study the silver issue, because as long as our country does not break away from the silver standard, the silver price issue is indeed a personal issue. There should be a permanent organization to continue the research, so as to avoid making hasty decisions when the time comes.

Ministry of Education's General Order Regarding the Examination and Registration Method for Film Scripts 201

The Ministry of Education issued a general order to the education departments and bureaus of each province and city, stating that, "According to Instruction No. 5822 of the Executive Yuan, 'Approved the public letter No. 5605 from the Secretariat of the National Government Civil Service Office, which states, "Approved the letter No. 18304 from the Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee, regarding the forwarding of the film script examination and registration method from the Central Propaganda Committee. Please investigate, forward, and instruct your subordinates to take note." After review and submission, it was approved to proceed. A letter was sent to inform and forward the documents, etc., and the attached method and form were sent to this office. Accordingly, after review and submission, the Chairman instructed to hand it over to the Executive Yuan,' etc. In addition to replying to the letter, the corresponding original documents are copied and forwarded to your department for notification and general notification. This order,' etc. Three copies of the original documents are copied and forwarded. Upon receipt of this, in addition to jointly ordering the Film Examination Committee to take note with the Ministry of Interior, the corresponding original attachments are copied and forwarded to your department and bureau for notification. This order includes one copy of the letter and one copy each of the method and form. Public Letter Secret No. 1834 from the Secretariat of the Central Executive Committee. We have recently received a letter from the Central Propaganda Committee stating that, 'In order to guide the film industry and encourage the talent of film script writers, this committee has specially formulated the Film Script Examination and Registration Method. In addition to this committee printing and distributing the method to party departments at all levels for forwarding to film companies and film script writers for compliance, film companies are instructed to note that from the date of promulgation of this method, all film scripts that have not been examined and registered by this committee must not be made into films. Accordingly, two copies of the method are enclosed. We hope you will investigate, forward, and instruct the subordinates of the National Government to take note,' etc. Approved after review by the Standing Committee, the original attachments are specially enclosed and forwarded. We hope you will investigate, forward, and handle accordingly. To the Civil Service Office of the National Government, attached are one copy each of the method and form."

Film Script Examination and Registration Method 202

Article 1: The Central Propaganda Committee (hereinafter referred to as "this Committee") has established a Film Script Examination Committee under the Film Industry Guidance Committee to guide the film industry and encourage the talent of film script writers. Article 2: Film companies (regardless of Chinese or foreign capital) or individuals established within the territory of the Republic of China must submit their planned film scripts for examination and registration in accordance with the examination methods of this Committee. Article 3: The examination of film scripts is divided into preliminary examination and re-examination. Only film scripts that have undergone the above two procedures may be approved for registration. Article 4: When applying for preliminary examination, the following items should be specified: (1) Name of the film script; (2) Abstract of the film script (including the source of the script, synopsis, segments, songs, and music); (3) Name, address, and occupation of the screenwriter. Article 5: After the preliminary examination of the film script is approved, the applicant will be formally notified in writing by this Committee to compile the film script into a formal film script and submit it to this Committee for re-examination with the following items specified: (1) Film script (including scenes, shots, subtitles, dialogues, songs, actions, etc.); (2) Name and address of the applicant; (3) Name and address of the director; (4) List of actors and staff; (5) Filming location; (6) Release date; (7) Production costs. Article 6: Applicants for preliminary and re-examination of film scripts may submit applications simultaneously. Article 7: Film scripts applying for examination should pay fees in accordance with the following methods: A. For film scripts applying for preliminary examination, a fee of one yuan per film will be charged. B. For film scripts applying for re-examination, a fee of three yuan per film will be charged. Article 8: If the name and plot of a film script applying for preliminary examination are inconsistent, or if the plot is inappropriate, the original work may be returned to the author to be revised in accordance with the opinion of this Committee, or it may be revised by this Committee. If the entire plot violates the provisions of Article 2 of the Film Examination Law, this Committee may not examine it. Article 9: Film scripts that have been approved for registration by this Committee after re-examination will be issued a registration certificate by this Committee. Article 10: If a film script applying for examination and registration has special significance and meets the standards stipulated by the Central Government, it may be rewarded by this Committee. The method will be determined separately. Article 11: Film scripts may only be made into films after being approved for registration by this Committee after examination. The registered scripts will also be sent to the Ministry of Education and the Film Examination Committee of the Ministry of Interior for reference to facilitate inspection. Article 12: Film scripts that have been approved for registration by this Committee or rewarded by this Committee may be advertised and promoted externally. Article 13: This method will be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Chairman Chiang Kai-shek Serves as Chairman of the Zhejiang Boy Scout Congress 203

Cultivating the Seeds of National Revival

Opening Ceremony Scheduled for Children's Day in Hangzhou

The Boy Scout movement in Zhejiang Province has shown considerable progress in recent years. The third annual congress will open in Hangzhou on Children's Day. The Party and government authorities believe that the position of chairman should be held by Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, a native of the province who serves as a role model for young people. Upon receiving the news, Chairman Chiang immediately telegraphed his acceptance. With the congress approaching, preparations are actively underway. It is also said that the main events of this activity include life skills competitions (divided into four categories: food, clothing, housing, and transportation), skill competitions (divided into seventeen categories: first aid, single flag semaphore, double flag semaphore, bridge building, platform construction, bicycle, rope tying, fire starting, military stick use, knife and axe use, shooting, surveying, climbing, sewing, singing, bugle, reconnaissance, etc.), production exhibitions (divided into woodworking, metalworking, bamboo working, mud working, carving, photography, drawing, weaving, embroidery, etc.), literary and artistic exhibitions (divided into treatises, diaries, stories, narratives, dramas, poetry, etc.), and other activities such as inspections, parades, lantern processions, campfires, boating, mountain climbing, service, visits, and various meetings.

Zhejiang University Plans to Build New School Buildings 204

All to be Completed Within Four Years

Total Cost of 1.2 Million

Zhejiang University finds its existing campus on Daxue Road too small and inadequate. Furthermore, as it is surrounded by residential buildings, expansion is difficult. Therefore, there is a proposal to move the entire university to a centralized location outside Taiping Gate for construction. The new site has now been surveyed and determined. Construction of the College of Agriculture building is scheduled to begin in March and be completed by the end of September. The cost of its laboratories, classrooms, dormitories, and other buildings is estimated to be 300,000 yuan. After the completion of the College of Agriculture building, the remaining buildings will be constructed in order. It is said that the university's construction plan is divided into two phases. The first phase includes the Mathematics and Physics Building, Biology Building, Chemistry Building, Agriculture Building, and Library, which are to be completed within four years, with an estimated cost of 1.2 million yuan. The second phase includes the Auditorium, Gymnasium, Office Building, Infirmary, Faculty and Staff Dormitories, Student Dormitories, and Dining Hall, which will commence after the completion of the first phase. As for the construction funds, in addition to striving to tighten budgets internally, the university will also request subsidies from the central government and various agencies.

Jiangsu Provincial Yancheng Middle School Keen on Construction 205

Since Wu Dezhang took over as headmaster of Jiangsu Provincial Yancheng Middle School last autumn, many improvements have been made, and the school's reputation in society has been growing daily. Detailed information has already been reported in various newspapers in Nanjing and Shanghai. However, as the school was founded not long ago, its history is still shallow, and its facilities are simple and makeshift in many respects. Headmaster Wu deeply believes that the excellence of students' academic performance, in addition to serious teaching and strict discipline, also requires attention to facilities, as the environment is quite sufficient to influence students' interest in learning. Therefore, in addition to building a laboratory last autumn, the school's campus, except for the city wall on the east side serving as a barrier, only has ditches as natural boundaries on the south, west, and north sides. However, the narrow stream of water gradually dries up after autumn, not only is the defense insufficient, but also the management is hampered by the lack of strictness. Therefore, during the winter vacation, based on the above two reasons, he submitted a request to the Education Department for funds to build a wall, which has been approved and construction has begun, and will be completed soon. Furthermore, as the school still lacks a self-study room, special classrooms, a covered playground, and an auditorium, preparations are also underway to formulate plans and submit requests for construction, prioritizing the most urgent needs, to ensure that the facilities are substantial and the environment is beautiful, so as to suit the students' concentrated study. In addition, the school is also gradually realizing its plans to purchase a large batch of books, build an animal pavilion, and develop a goldfish pond, all of which can beautify the campus and entertain the mind and body. This shows Wu's keen determination to build and reform education.

Tongji University Holds Memorial Service for Ottmann, Dean of Studies at the Attached High School 209

Mr. Ottmann, Dean of Studies at the Attached High School of National Tongji University, returned to Germany for convalescence last year due to cancer and unfortunately passed away in Göttingen in December. Details were previously published in this newspaper. The school deeply mourned his death, as Mr. Ottmann had taught for over a decade with tireless dedication. A memorial service was held on the morning of February 28th to express their grief. Attendees included the German Consul-General, Director of the Public Works Bureau Shen Junyi, all the Chinese and German professors and students, and over a thousand friends of Mr. Ottmann. Dr. Weng Zhilong, the president of the university, delivered a speech, stating that Mr. Ottmann was loyal to his duties, diligent in his work, and admired by his colleagues. He was enthusiastic about the expansion and equipment of Tongji University. His efforts during the January 28th Incident, his appeals, and his rescue plans were particularly moving. In addition to his studies in literature and philosophy, he was also proficient in linguistics and could speak English, French, Greek, Latin, Hebrew, and various Indian languages. He was particularly interested in Chinese language and literature and had made profound achievements. He had written books such as "Common Spoken Language of Northern China" and the "German-Chinese Dictionary." The "German-Chinese Dictionary" was a significant contribution to literature. Unfortunately, the manuscript was submitted to the Commercial Press during the January 28th Incident and was destroyed. Since then, no one has continued his work. Mr. Ottmann had a deep understanding of Confucian doctrines and promoted Chinese culture to Europe. Mr. Ottmann can be regarded as a leader in this field. Therefore, his death is not only a great loss to Tongji University, but it is also closely related to the communication of Chinese and German culture. Finally, he said that our commemoration of Mr. Ottmann is not only a mourning, but also a memorial to express our eternal grief, which will be discussed further. Afterwards, the German Consul-General, the deans of the medical and engineering colleges, the director of the attached high school, representatives of the faculty and staff, representatives of the students, representatives of the German-Austrian-Swiss Alumni Association, and representatives of the Tongji Alumni Association, Shen Junyi, and Chen Heming delivered speeches, followed by a thank-you speech by a representative of the family.

Initiating a Memorial Service for Chen Qubing 210

To be Held at the Ningbo Fellow-Villagers Association on the Afternoon of the 4th at 3 PM

Mr. Chen Qubing of Wujiang was a revolutionary elder, a leading figure in the Southern Society, and his moral character and literary talent made great contributions to the Party and the country. His unfortunate passing has been mourned throughout the world. (1) Punishment

(2) The President of Jiaotong University will automatically issue a written apology to the Referees Association and Shen Huichun. (3) Jiaotong University will compensate Shen Huichun for medical expenses of 200 yuan.

(4) Compensation for litigation costs of 600 yuan.

(5) The plaintiff and defendant will jointly request the prosecutor to withdraw the public prosecution.

(6) Shen Huichun will not file any further civil lawsuits.

Ambiguity in Football Rules 230

The Goalpost Falls and the Ball Enters the Goal

Explanation from the British Referees Association

(Reuters, London) Recently, the British Football Committee received a report from the Referees Association at a meeting regarding the interpretation of Article 4 of the football regulations, which was requested by the Westlaw Association. The article is as follows:

"During the game, if the goalpost falls due to any accident, the referee may award a goal if, in his opinion, the ball would have passed under the goalpost if it had not fallen."

The Referees Association stated that only if the goalpost falls and, in the referee's opinion, the ball would have passed under the goalpost at that time if it had not fallen, then the referee has the right to award a goal. If the goalpost falls and cannot be reinstalled, then the game is canceled.

Fifth Guangzhou City Ring Road Race 233

Total Distance of 15,079 Meters

Champion Zhao Hui's Time: 58 Minutes 51 Seconds

(Guangzhou Dispatch) The annual Guangzhou City Ring Road Public Race was held for the fifth time this year on the 24th in the bright spring sunshine. The Provincial Sports Committee had made thorough arrangements beforehand, and hospitals were requested to send ambulance teams to escort the runners along the route. Scouts and military police from various schools were dispatched to maintain order along the route. When the long-distance runners passed, traffic was temporarily stopped, and pedestrians were not allowed to cross at major intersections. Dozens of stations were set up along the route, with two to three judges stationed at each station to maintain order. If an athlete stopped during the race, the judges and guards had the right to confiscate their number. The confiscated numbers were reported to the judges at the finish line, and the offending athletes were taken to the escort vehicle and not allowed to continue the race. The starting and finishing points of the race were both at the Provincial Public Sports Field in the eastern suburbs. Citizens flocked to watch the race. A horizontal banner reading "Fifth Guangzhou Public City Ring Road Race" was hung in front of the venue. At around 11:00 AM, the athletes who had registered gathered at the venue. The starter, Qiu Jixiang, gathered the male champion Zhao Hui and female champion Gao Xiaodie, checked their numbers, explained the precautions for the race to the athletes, and finally called their names one by one. There were 188 male athletes and 4 female athletes. After the roll call, the chairman of the meeting, Xie Yingzhou, fired the starting gun, and the athletes set off. They first ran three laps around the track in the Public Sports Field, and then set off on the avenue. The Public Security Bureau inspectors led the way in a tram. The streets were crowded with spectators, and the scouts and military police maintained order very well. After the athletes had passed, traffic was restored to that section of the road. The route started from Dadong Road and passed through Huiai Road, Fengning Road, Lupai Road, Cunshan Road, Shiwufu Road, Datong Road, 623 Road, Xiti, Taiping South Road, Yide Road, Taikang Road, Wanfu Road, Yuexiu South Road, Baiyun Road, Dongchuan Road, and back to Dadong Road Public Sports Field, where they ran one more lap around the track to determine the winner. The entire course was 30.92 li, equivalent to 15,079 meters. On the day of the race, the athletes initially conserved their strength, and the distances between them were small. As they ran past the halfway point, those who could not keep up gradually dropped out, and more than half were eliminated. By the time they reached Yide Road, one of the female athletes was exhausted and fainted. The ambulance team rescued her and put her on the vehicle. As they approached Baiyun Road, the stronger male athletes began to exert themselves. Zhao Hui, a student from Zhongshan University and a former champion, used his remaining strength to move forward, advancing from the sixteenth or seventeenth position to the front. Huang Zhizhong, an athlete from the 8th Division, who had been leading the way, was overtaken by Zhao. Although Huang struggled to catch up, it was too late. Soon after, when they ran back to the Public Sports Field, Zhao Hui was still in the lead, with the correct posture. When he reached the finish line, the timekeeper announced that the race time was 58 minutes 51.4 seconds. Huang Zhizhong (athlete from the 8th Division of the 3rd Army), the second-place winner, arrived shortly after, with a time of 59 minutes 15 seconds. Zhou Feng (athlete from the 7th Division of the 3rd Army) came in third, Liu Biao (athlete from the Police Fire Brigade) came in fourth, and Xu Guoping (athlete from the Headquarters Military Band) came in fifth. Ten minutes after the first-place winner arrived, thirty-four athletes had reached the finish line. Sixty-one athletes were able to run the entire course. The female champion Gao Xiaodie's time was 84 minutes 47 seconds. The runner-up was Li Xuehua, and the third-place winner was Lan Qianqiong. The above three female athletes are all students from physical education schools. After the rankings were determined, the chairman, Xie Yingzhou, gave a speech to the winners, and then presented the awards on the spot. After that, a football performance was held to celebrate. The opposing teams were Lingnan School and the Air Force. The performance was very exciting. The event ended at around 3:00 PM. The past results are attached below:

1920: Zhao Hui, 11,338 meters, 45 minutes

1921: Zhao Hui, 13,248 meters, 50 minutes 16.3 seconds

1922: Yuan Yucheng, 15,079 meters, 57 minutes 24.4 seconds

1923: Zhao Hui, 15,079 meters, 58 minutes 20 seconds

1924: Zhao Hui, 15,079 meters, 58 minutes 51.4 seconds

Spring and Autumn

Praising the Dead 234

— Be Careful What You Say

The Chinese have a habit of liking to put on a show for the dead. An ordinary person, after their death, is often praised as if they were a truly remarkable figure. For example, large obituaries that are more than two or three inches thick, grand funerals that block an entire road, and opening memorial halls and holding Taoist ceremonies for every seventh day after death are all, strictly speaking, ways of praising the dead. However, because the praiser and the praised are either father and son or husband and wife, there is always some kind of familial relationship. Therefore, even though those on the sidelines know that this is obviously a case of "farting after the horse passes," using the praising of the dead as a pretext to promote oneself, it doesn't feel too nauseating. The most nauseating thing is when a group of unrelated people, after the peaceful death of someone who is seemingly famous but actually unknown, follow the lead of a few people who have a slight relationship with the deceased and publish articles praising them or her in the newspaper day and night.

Although this trend has been around for a long time, it has become even worse now!

A certain poet died, and before his death, absolutely no one mentioned him. After his death, many publications actually put out special issues for him. Perhaps the editors of these publications had repeatedly rejected the poet's submissions with extremely cold faces while he was alive! Perhaps because the poet was not as famous as Xu Zhimo, many people were "using the word 'poet'" to mock him while he was alive. After his death, these many people immediately changed their tone and used terms such as "my friend" or "China's modern poet" to sincerely write articles praising him!

Recently, Ai Xia, a film actress who was not very famous during her lifetime and only occasionally wrote a few articles, died. As soon as this news spread, articles praising the dead appeared in newspapers like a tidal wave. If someone were to cut them all out and print a "Book of Condolences," I think it would be at least as thick as the Shen Bao Yearbook. And from then on, Ai Xia's reputation would almost surpass that of Hu Die and Chen Yumei, but she is already dead!

It is precisely because this person is dead that we want to praise them. It is precisely because this person is already dead that they will no longer be an obstacle to us, so we can praise them without fear!

Alas! Cold-hearted people! Why are you unwilling to give a person some more substantial help while they are alive?

The Mystery of Prophecy 235

— Qing Qu

"Prophecy" has almost become an unfathomable mystery. If you don't believe it and dismiss it as decadent and declining Chinese scholarship and the idle words that emerge from intellectual turmoil, then what about foreign figures like H.G. Wells, Smuts, Arthur Balfour, and others who are universally recognized as "prophecy experts"? They are even revered as "saints of prophecy," which shows that it is not without basis. However, the shallow-minded are lurking in a state of ignorance and confusion, unable to awaken. Therefore, they never know any catastrophe beforehand, but only understand when disaster strikes, and then it is too late to avoid it!

I will leave aside major world events such as wars and focus on the current puppet state of Manchuria. Isn't it said that a Mr. Puyi will usurp the throne on March 1st? Alas! This matter reminds me of when Empress Dowager Longyu issued the edict of abdication in the ×th month of the first year of the Republic of China. Puyi had been on the throne for only three years, twelve months, and five days. From the entry of his ancestor, Emperor Taizu of the Qing dynasty, into China, he had ruled China for a total of ten generations, spanning 268 years. Until Puyi's abdication, that was the end of the Qing dynasty. The Jue Luo clan's demise can be considered an unprecedented occurrence since ancient times! But unexpectedly, the September 18th Incident occurred, and after the Japanese invaders occupied Liaoning and Jilin, figures such as Doihara, Zheng Xiaoxu, Jin Liang, Xi Qia, and Zhang Hai Peng appeared. Puyi was originally lying low in Zhang Yuan, playing tennis and not stepping out of Tianjin. Hey! Now he had to go to Dalian to take up this task. Although he was under the control of the Japanese puppet organization, he was naturally willing to fall into their trap to relive his imperial dream.

The day before yesterday, I met an old friend who returned from outside the customs. He said that this Mr. Puyi would soon usurp the throne. He believed that this was consistent with two lines from the prophecy of the "Yellow Bitter Gourd Zen poem": "Jiantong dwells in a small corner for thirty-six years, watching the blood like hemp beyond the border." "Jiantong" is the Xuantong era. At first, the Japanese Doihara and others wanted to establish a "Mingguang Empire" in the three northeastern provinces, but they were unsuccessful. After they took Puyi out of the customs, today they have the "Kangde" reign. "Thirty-six" corresponds to the World War, which must begin in 1936. At that time, the so-called puppets in Manchuria, like wooden dummies, will be manipulated by others and correspond to the blood like hemp beyond the border. The only way out is to sit and wait for death. There is no other way. To expect to be as safe as during the fall of the Qing dynasty, hey! That is truly dreaming in the dark! Although these words are close to the talk of prophecy experts, a careful examination reveals some precognitive predictions. I am afraid that they will not be able to escape this fate!

Pink Existence 236

— Jue

The love between a patron and a prostitute is guaranteed by money. A friend who was disappointed in love sighed and said, "I never thought that the current love arena would be like this!"

Chasing, watching movies, and opening hotels are the first three movements of love; falling in love, getting married, and getting divorced are the last three movements of love.

First love is intoxication, love is sweetness, and long love is boredom. This is what people who have experienced love say.

A man expresses love to a woman by giving her a diamond ring; a woman expresses love to a man with a burst of charming laughter.

Miss, female student, vase, young mistress, mother, old woman, old lady, a girlfriend said to me: This process is the typical life of a woman.

Literati 237

— Zhang Bingduo

Locked tightly by the chains of life, almost suffocating, with tens of bushels of burdens weighing down on my whole body, when I look at my face in a broken old mirror, the yellow-black skin, the thin cheekbones, the hair so disheveled, the pupils in the two sunken eyes so lifeless and weak, I never thought that after only three to five months of floating and struggling in the city, I would unconsciously lose my former handsome appearance.

In this era, literati are cheaper than a tail-wagging dog begging for food. Poverty and despair, an excess of knowledge cannot be exchanged for a fried dough stick or half a loaf of bread. I rack my brains and pour out my heart and soul to write articles, and after finally getting them published, I receive eight or nine yuan a month, which is barely enough to eat. I still have to pay for postage, laundry, haircuts... Indeed, life is really hard!

Every day, regardless of whether it is sunny or rainy, and at dusk, writing articles under a dim light is such a painful and unbearable thing. But if I don't write, my stomach will panic. Writing means pouring out my heart and soul every day, which is truly unspeakable suffering. And where will I get so much material? In addition, the so-called modern ladies next door, who have nothing to do after filling their stomachs, are always humming a series of seductive tunes, disturbing my mind so that it cannot be clear. At night, the Shanghai opera on the radio will be noisy until twelve o'clock, and the sound of cars speeding by reminds me of the sighs and curses I have for the leisure class. I cannot continue to write.

In this era, literati have fallen to the most unfortunate and lowest point. The pampered dog sitting next to the young master and young lady may have a more comfortable and stable life. In fact, if it weren't for a little bit of meager payment to maintain my life and prolong my existence, who would be patient enough to happily pour out their heart and soul to win a little appreciation from the leisure class!

Brief News: The Siming Series edited and engraved by Mr. Zhang Yongni, owner of Yuanyuan Garden, has been reprinted by 5,000 copies due to strong sales. The second collection of 22 books will be published within this month. The book is engraved in imitation of Bao's Zhībùzú Zhai Series. Pre-ordering the second collection costs 40 yuan, and purchasing both the first and second collections together reduces the price to 80 yuan. Managed by the China Bookstore on Sanma Road.
