Little Knowledge

Common Sense on Saving Electricity 238

— Su

After the American scientist Thomas Edison invented the electric light in 1879 in the Western calendar, it soon spread around the world. Now even the slightly larger cities in our country have traces of it. Especially in the most prosperous Shanghai, we spend every night with it, and it has become one of our daily necessities. Moreover, the monthly electricity bill is a major daily expense, just like the water bill, and we certainly need to find ways to save on it. Now I will write down the three methods I know separately below for the readers' reference.

1. Check the Voltage

The voltage of each light bulb is marked with numbers on the bulb's base. Commonly used ones are 200 volts because the voltage of the incoming wires is also the same, which is specified by the transformer. If the voltage of the light bulb is too low, the filament is easily burned out. If the voltage is too high, the light will not be bright. Therefore, it is best to use a 200-volt light bulb, which has strong light and is also cost-effective.

2. Replace the Light Bulb

Ordinary light bulbs lose their effectiveness after being used for eight or nine months (assuming four hours of use per day). This is because the filament is burned out by the high heat generated by the electric current. However, after five months, the filament has gradually dissolved into vapor and attached to the bulb, making the light dimmer day by day. At this time, it is necessary to add more lights to restore the previous brightness. The added electricity bill is consumed by the old bulb. Therefore, it is very cost-effective to replace the light bulb after five or six months of use.

3. Use Half-Watt Bulbs

As mentioned earlier, ordinary light bulbs become dim after being used for a certain period of time. However, there is now a way to remedy this. That is, by injecting nitrogen or argon gas into the vacuum bulb, the filament can be melted more slowly. This kind of bulb is called a nitrogen bulb or an argon bulb. Also, because this light bulb only needs half a watt of electricity per candlepower, it is also called a Half-Watt Lamp. Various electrical stores in Shanghai sell them. Although the price is about twice as expensive as ordinary bulbs, they are very durable and save a lot of electricity. For example, when using a 200-volt ordinary bulb and a half-watt bulb, each consuming 100 watts of electricity, the ordinary bulb can only emit 87 candlepower, while the half-watt bulb can emit 200 candlepower, which is more than twice the light power of the ordinary bulb. Therefore, using half-watt bulbs is indeed a very electricity-saving thing.

The above three methods are all things I have tried and they are very effective. Please feel free to try them as well. If you install a few light bulbs at home, the savings are of course limited. However, if you install dozens or hundreds of light bulbs, the amount will be very large. This is also a way to reduce spending in household economics.

Hope Everyone Does This 239

— Zou Ronghe

Many of the people in Chinese society who are unemployed and complaining are young people; however, the people who can achieve something are also only young people. Therefore, we came forward in the past to organize a Living Society. Now I will write down our present and future below, hoping to be corrected. There are a total of ten of us. Five of us are temporarily teachers. We each receive 15 yuan from our earnings as living expenses, and the rest is used as capital. For the five months from April, we now have a rented house, six mu of rented fields, one head of yellow cattle, two boxes of bees, and more than a hundred chickens of various sizes. We plan to use all of our teaching income as capital after the autumn of next year. Three years later, all of us will join in, from farming to forestry. Five years later, our parents, younger siblings can also join in to do chores like tending fire and herding livestock. After ten years, we should have more than 20,000 yuan of capital that is worth investing. Now I will write down the general idea of ​​the organization.

Each person only has living expenses and no salary.

Except for unavoidable expenses, all food and accommodation are made by ourselves.

Each person spends two hours reading and half an hour teaching the children in the village and neighborhood.

Within five years, one person will visit industries in the country in order to develop them.

After ten years, we can provide funds for studying abroad.

Each year, each person plants hundreds of camphor trees and investigates the local mineral resources.

We hope that all the weak young people in the country will practice this and become useful farmers.

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 240

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 25: Tearful faces bid farewell to family and return to distant garrison / Wind and sand fill the night as they leave the border and station in a lonely city

When Ziqiang turned his head, he realized that his father and mother-in-law had both come to see him off at the gate. At this point, no matter how tough Ziqiang's heart was, he couldn't just ignore them. He had to turn around and run back to his father, bowing to the old man and saying, "Don't see me off, father. I will be fine." As he spoke, he saw some dust on his father's shoulder, so he reached out and gently patted his father's shoulder. Zhao Weng held his dry tobacco pipe, looked at him, coughed twice, and nodded, saying, "Alright, go ahead." Jiang stood by the door frame, holding her own collar, and said to Ziqiang, "Son-in-law, take care of yourself. I will take care of things at home." What else could Ziqiang say? He only pressed his hands to his chest and kept bowing to everyone. Guizhi was still standing far ahead, calling out, "Hurry to the station, don't miss the time." Ziqiang was an old soldier, and he had already developed the habits of a soldier. At this time, he was outside the gate, so he naturally straightened his chest and gave a military salute. Then he stood upright, turned around, and left. This time he was determined and didn't turn his head back to look. Guizhi followed behind, walking with big steps, counting "one, two, three, four" in her mouth. Their house was not far from the long-distance bus station, only one turn away. When he stopped, Guizhi smiled and said, "You are a soldier, how can you be so indecisive? At the time of parting, you just kept pulling and tugging." Ziqiang sighed, immediately straightened his chest again, and smiled, "You are right, we must show some manly demeanor." Xiaolin put his luggage down beside him and suddenly asked, "Company Commander, are you rushing back to Xifengkou this time because there is going to be a battle soon?" How could Ziqiang answer this question? Even Guizhi knew in her heart that this might be the case in reality, but she always hoped that it wouldn't be so, so she went around and around, and never said such a thing. (325)

Free Talk

Knife and Pen 241

— Hu Ran

An Indian revolutionary once asked someone from × country: "Did you conquer India with a knife or a pen? If with a pen, then India can strive for freedom; if with a knife, then even if India is not martial, it can still strive for freedom by breaking bones as weapons." Wise words!

These words are very sad! Under heavy oppression and restraint, hope gradually turns from big to small, and from small to nothing. In the hopelessness of despair, many great hearts turn to ashes, and boiling blood turns to cold blood. However, after the hermit Rādha went into meditation for several years, he was suddenly shaken awake by someone using a method. At this time, he ascended into the void, making great divine transformations, setting himself on fire, and even the dead ashes and cold blood disappeared. This became a precedent for many reformers.

It is not difficult to answer this kind of desperate cry. It is neither a knife nor a pen, but rather to create preparations for India to obtain freedom. This kind of talk can be perfunctory for a while and can lull children back to sleep. Whatever kind of Chinese thing it is, Westerners only need to add the words "leased territory" to make us feel at peace. In short, the great benevolence and righteousness of × country is nothing more than temporarily managing India for the Indians.

But what is the answer? From an outsider's point of view, both knife and pen are used. For example, the murderer is the knife; the charges after the murder are the pen. The announcement of punishment is the pen; the mobilization of troops is the knife. After × country uses military methods to conquer India, it must use literary methods to manage it. At this time, of course, there will be various great principles that should be obeyed by the people of × country, either hypnotizing, or anesthetizing, or adopting a pessimistic view. What if they still don't submit to the rule under these circumstances? It's very simple, use the knife again. Just like when a child wakes up at night and doesn't want to sleep, the adult should try to coax them to sleep. What if the coaxing skills are exhausted? Then hit them.

However, it is still not very effective. Historically, one can always see rotating changes, and rarely see a consistent linear progression. The old saying goes that people and heaven are closely connected. Since heaven is endless, then the human heart is also endless. After turning into a state of sadness or heartbreak, breaking bones can be used as weapons, and self-strangulation can also be done. This further proves the immeasurability of heaven's will and the human heart, and that the world has never been calm.

Talking About "Taiping Song" 242

— Mu Mutian

The "Lantern Festival" has arrived, which can't help but remind me of the "Taiping Song" in my hometown.

In my childhood, two kinds of local art gave me a deep impression. One was donkey shadow puppetry, and the other was "Taiping Song". Of course, drum songs and scripts also gave me considerable interest, but "Taiping Song" and donkey shadow puppetry gave me a stronger impression. This may be because the local and popular nature of these two things is relatively strong.

During festivals, these two things give the people great happiness. It is not limited to towns, but is widespread to various villages. In terms of responding to the festive season, donkey shadow puppetry can be performed at any time, while "Taiping Song" can only be sung during the first month of the lunar year. Perhaps it is a kind of performance to welcome the spring. When performing donkey shadow puppetry and singing "Taiping Song", the villages are really crowded and extremely lively. In the summer of 1930, I also watched the last donkey shadow puppetry in Jiangnan, Jilin Provincial City, but the audience was not as enthusiastic as before. As for "Taiping Song", because of "leaving my hometown at a young age", I have not had the opportunity to appreciate it for more than twenty years.

Donkey shadow puppetry is also known as Luanzhou shadow puppetry. It was probably transplanted to "Guandong City" by Luanzhou merchants. In the past, 90% of the Northeast's commerce was in the hands of people from Changli, Laoting, Luanzhou, and Funing counties. So, donkey shadow puppetry can be regarded as a foreign art in the Northeast. "Taiping Song" is a native art of the Northeast. According to my friend Mr. Hu, shadow puppetry is an art of the Luanhe River basin, while "Taiping Song" is an art of the Liaohe River basin.

"Taiping Song" is also known as "Yangge". Villagers say "sing Yangge". When written on paper, it is "Taiping Song". At the beginning of the New Year, people who are "competitive" start preparing for "Yangge". Naturally, this requires the support of gentry and rich people. After the land is harvested, the grain is sold, and what is stored is stored. When a year of work is completed, during the celebration of the New Year, those competitive people who like to help others organize "Yangge troupes" to celebrate the future year of "longevity and abundance". "Yangge" is a costumed parade dance. Responding to the rhythm of the music of gongs, drums, cymbals, and nao, thirty or twenty people, or forty or fifty people, dressed in various costumes of men, women, old and young, make a circle, walking and dancing in circles. At a certain interval of time, periodically, the band stops the music, the dancers stop jumping, and one person comes out from the line, opens a fan, faces upwards, and sings a "Yangge tune" like a seven-character quatrain. When the first three sentences are sung, a burst of music is played. When the last sentence is sung, it is music and dance again.

During the lively season, "Yangge" is "performing" in the center of the street or village, and the audience is naturally surrounding it. In general times, "Yangge" circulates through various shops and families, and the audience follows behind, walking around to watch. In the courtyards of each family, "Yangge" performs, dances, and sings for about ten minutes or twenty minutes, depending on the situation. The songs sung are mostly congratulations to the shops for making money and the gentry and rich people for the prosperity of their families. For the families of officials, of course, they celebrate promotion, and for the local gentry and rich people, they celebrate a year of abundance. The gentry and merchants usually give generous rewards.

In the costumes of "Yangge", there is "Old Tartar", wearing a foreign fur robe backwards, with copper jingle bells on his body, and "Big-footed Wife", who is a man dressed as a woman, like a middle-aged woman. There are others, but I can't remember.

Many of the "Yangge tunes" are readily available, such as "In the Twelfth Month" and "Picking Tea in the Twelfth Month", etc. The form is mostly four sentences of seven characters. However, there are also newly made ones, which the singer improvises according to the occasion. Let me write down a few that I remember:

"Entering the gate and looking up, I see the lantern pole above, on the lantern pole are four big characters, (music) abundant harvest and peaceful year."

"Cherries are delicious but the tree is hard to plant, Yangge is good to sing but the mouth is hard to open, to eat cherries you have to spend money to buy them, (music) to sing Yangge you have to smear your face."

"In the first month, the first month is right, Bai Ma Yin Qiang Xiao Luocheng, everyone says Luocheng is small, (music) night fight Denzhou to save Qin Qiong."

"In the second month, the dragon raises its head, the Emperor Wansui comes to use the ox, the Queen Mother comes to deliver food, (music) whip the plough ox for ten thousand years of harvest."

"Entering the gate, dong dong dong, your old courtyard is like Beijing, the main room is like the Golden Luan Palace, (music) the courtyard wall is like the Forbidden City."

The first four songs are readily available, and the last one is improvised.

Seeing Mr. Zheng Zhenduo's "Ancient Book Discovery in 1933" mentioned "shadow words", I thought of this folk art "Yangge tune" in the Liaohe River basin, and felt that this rich treasure trove is worthy of the attention of scholars and literati. The arrival of the "Lantern Festival" further makes me feel the need to arouse people's attention to this treasure trove. I don't know if there is also this kind of "Taiping Song" in other provinces in the mainland. However, in the future, after the Liaohe River basin falls into the hands of the Yi Di, perhaps the trampling of iron hooves will cause this kind of literature and art to perish, so that it will be lost. We should collect "Yangge tunes" as soon as possible. The difficulty is that this kind of thing does not seem to have a copy. Most of it still relies on oral transmission.

Gurkha 243

—

Gurkha is an important place on the border between Yunnan and Burma, located in the Savage Mountains. Going south from the Luanxian Street of Qianya Dam in Yunnan, it takes half a day's walk through the mountains to reach it. There, there are no streets, no villages, only a small mountain ditch, flowing out of the mountains with green trees and verdant bamboos, and flowing into the dense cliffs and thickets again. The border treaty at the end of the Guangxu period divided Burma and China by means of this mountain ditch. A Western-style iron bridge stood over the mountain ditch, dazzlingly marking the civilized style of the twentieth century. Beside the mountain ditch, there was a small savage thatched hut, and all the shadows of the primitive era still remained.

Leaning on the railing on the bridge, the smooth mountain road wound to the south, paved with white fine stones, showing the cleanliness after the rain. Gray-green lead pillars stood on the side of the road, and the iron wires of the electric wires stretched across them, extending into the distant trees. When the mountain wind stirred, they made a buzzing sound. Thinking about walking into those mountains in Southern Europe, the scenery in front of the traveler's eyes is probably nothing more than this, right? At the same time, looking back to the north, the mountain road is rugged and accumulated with mud after the rain. No matter who looks at it, it is inevitable to sigh at the difficulty of walking. The electric wires connected to Chinese cities are also not lacking, but the electric poles are made of thick bamboo poles, which look quite shabby. Fortunately, at that time, I didn't have much hope for China, so in contrast, I didn't feel any sentiment at all. Just like a thorough wanderer, I happily stepped into a fresh environment.

That year, when I arrived here, it was noon after a light rain. The sky suddenly cleared, and the surrounding mountains covered in green clothes were as fresh as after a bath. The fragrance of wild grass and tender branches floated everywhere in the air. The stream made a gurgling sound, flowing to the distance, and then dissolved into the quiet embrace of ten thousand mountains. At that time, I ate a meal made by the savages in the small thatched hut beside the bridge. Even now, when I think about it, I still find it quite interesting. At first, when I saw this only small thatched hut, no matter how humble it was, I always felt that in this environment where all I could see were mountains and green trees, it would reduce the traveler's loneliness in many ways. But later, when I lowered my head and went in, I found out what the owner was like, and my heart couldn't help but beat faster, as if I had walked into a black shop selling human meat buns. Because the owner had a long knife with a flat head hanging on his waist (wearing a knife is a custom of the savages, and every adult man must carry it. Even when they are soldiers, they never leave this ancestral long knife in addition to carrying a gun) and his face was naturally untamed. His two lips revealed a look as if he had just eaten human blood, because he often chewed betel nuts. The black cloth turban wrapped around his head had a section left over, standing straight on his hair, vividly depicting the demeanor of a hero of the green forest. Eating under the hospitality of such a host, and in the lonely ten thousand mountains, who can forget it? The dishes I ate that time, in addition to a bamboo tube with a light yellow vegetable soup, were a small bag of tree vegetables wrapped around [omitted] (I didn't dare to use chopsticks [omitted, said to be] to fill my stomach, because there were no chopsticks at all).

After the explanation of my traveling companion, I grabbed it and tasted it, and found it was unusually crisp and fragrant, and very delicious. When eating, there was no table, no凳子, just squatting on the ground like a beggar. After eating such a meal, I climbed to the western-style bridgehead, waved to the north, and said goodbye to China, and no emotion of reluctance welled up in my heart.

After crossing the bridge, not far away, beside the road, stretched another small black road, which led to the nearby military camp. Indian troops lived there, guarding the Burmese border, and at any time had the responsibility of expanding it.

Complaint 244

— Bai Yan

The mother grumbled with complaints; the wife shed tears.

The young husband's heart felt as if it were being twisted by a knife; he hung his head.

"Humph! No words to say! No rice in the jar, no firewood under the stove; you don't care about anything. As soon as you get your salary, you have to buy woolen socks for your wife first, afraid of freezing your precious wife!..." the mother said angrily. Then she sighed softly.

"I think, freezing won't kill anyone, not having food to eat is hard. Don't you think about it yourself: twenty or thirty yuan a month, what's that enough for? Everything is expensive now, you can't even take care of food and clothing, and you still want to spend it recklessly. When you're hungry, you'll only have to drink the northwest wind!..."

The mother saw that her son was drooping his head and looking dejected, so her tone seemed to soften a little.

The young husband's heart was filled with waves of regret, surging. He thought:

"Ah! Mother! How could I not understand the difficult situation at home? I also know that this money should be used to buy urgently needed supplies! But when I saw my [wife's] feet were so badly frozen that she couldn't even wear shoes: in this season of deep winter, she was still wearing single-thread socks, how could I bear it? You think, how can a person's skin withstand the severe cold? Moreover, these woolen socks didn't cost much money!"

However, he didn't dare to argue like this; he just let it simmer in his stomach.

The mother glanced at her son, propped her right hand on her chin; puffed out her cheeks; and snorted from her nostrils.

"...Humph! As the saying goes, "A mother is a roadside grass", a wife is still better." Loves his wife so much!...

He throws his mother behind his back.... the mother muttered to herself.

The young husband glanced sideways at his wife, remaining silent. The wife also just stared at the ground with distress.

………………

The room was filled with unpleasant air.

The young husband's heart felt as if it were being twisted by a knife, drooping his head.

The mother grumbled with complaints, the wife shed tears.

No Snow 245

— Miao Chongqun

—Scenery of Northern Country in 1933

Near the desert, when the wind blows, the sky is yellow.

Camels silently carry coal blocks from Mentougou. A good load is several hundred pieces, and two can carry more than a ton. There is no need for any heavy trucks, anyway, when they are transported to the city, they turn into smoke ash and slag.

Camels are in rows and columns. At the back of each row, there is always a small one; with a bell made of a foreign cigarette can hanging on its neck. When you hear the ding-dong sound, you know the camels are about to pass.

In winter, there is no snow, and in spring, you can't see any green grass. You don't step on the desert, you step on dust that is deeper than the ash in the incense burner. Those foreigners who live in the Legation Quarter, they are tired of the imperial palace, tired of Qianmen Street and the antiques on Morrison Street, sometimes they run up our city walls, with their Agfa or Kodak cameras, they aim the lens at rows of camels or scattered, messy, yellow-skinned people on the street and press the button. The so-called scenery in this ancient city is captured by them.

The locals don't understand what the Legation Quarter is, they just know that the place with gun emplacements and artillery forts is "West Jiaomin Lane".

Not only is there green grass in West Jiaomin Lane, but it is greener than anywhere else. The trees are also special, each one is painted with white lime, showing them to be so neat and clean.

Foreign dogs with short chestnut hair, their bodies glistening like satin. This luster is also the dignity of their owners. They have good nutrition, eating several pounds of beef and biscuits every day according to the rules. The owners work in big foreign buildings, and they stroll or wander outside, their lives are very leisurely.

When the weather is good, their eyes squint a little. On the grass or under the roots of trees, they can sniff the scent of the opposite sex, and no one cares about these things, as long as they are happy.

Standing on the post is a Chinese man, wearing yellow, Qing Dynasty-era short-筒靴子, holding a short警棍 in his hand. He is also very idle, looking at the grass, looking at the trees, looking at the foreign dogs, when he is lost in thought, he looks a little dull.

—Tomorrow I'll get my pay, he thought, the lunar calendar is already the fifth month, the festival is coming soon.

He lowered his head for a while, and soon turned it again, as if something had touched his mind.

Gently whistling,

—Sanbao, that little girl, is going to go up against me again.

Financial Silver Futures Rise Insignificantly, Gold Market Experiences Minor Correction 246

The situation is mostly sideways with a slight rebound to 5.8 yuan.

Yesterday, the gold market saw a slight correction due to the weak increase in silver futures. However, the overall situation remained sideways. In the morning, overseas silver markets in the UK and the US saw a unified surge, but silver futures only rose by a meager 0.06 to 0.022 taels. Exchange rates saw minimal fluctuations. London spot gold rose by six pence, American cotton rose slightly by three points, and American wheat decreased slightly by half a point. The opening price of the wool market was stable and then rose to 41.12 yuan. After opening, banks initially hoarded and then released, with HSBC listing British currency at par and American currency down 0.0125. As a result, gold prices briefly turned from weak to firm. However, banks took advantage of the high prices to release their holdings, Jewish merchants and Qiaozhi just released US dollars, Sassoon aggressively sold shillings, and the Central Bank also dumped US dollars, leading to a loosening of the domestic market and a sudden decline in confidence, with prices dropping to over 11 yuan. The afternoon market opened flat, with wavering confidence and minor corrections from time to time. However, due to strong buying interest from banks and the Central Bank's intermittent intervention, gold prices managed to rebound. Trading in March futures was lackluster, briefly breaking into 700 yuan territory, but ultimately remained stable. The day lacked major news, causing some confusion. The Central Bank opened spot trading in the morning, with 70 bars of Taikang Run and 35 bars of Dadecheng priced at 941.5 yuan, equivalent to a pure gold price of 953.5 yuan. The day's market conditions are summarized below.

The morning opening price was 940.7 yuan, up 3.2 yuan from the previous close. Goods opened at 0.08 yuan. The exchange rate opened in the morning with recent selling prices of 1 shilling 4.5625 pence for British currency and 35 yuan for US currency. Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Talk

Suicide 284

— Ya Fei

On the desk sits a set of calendars from the 23rd year of the Republic of China; although only a little over fifty pages have been turned – not even two months have passed – nevertheless, the number of suicide cases that have occurred has already exceeded twenty, and most of them involve young men and women. Examining the reasons for their suicides, they are nothing more than economic hardship, romantic issues, and failure in education. In particular, the recent cases of Hu Zhen, Yan Xiu'e, Wu Jilan, Ai Xia, and an unidentified glamorous corpse caused a sensation for a time. They suddenly seemed to have thrown a huge rock into this normally calm Shanghai society, stirring up ripples!

Ai Xia was a movie star and a talented writer. Wu Jilan was a famous female performer of Peking Opera, with considerable literary cultivation. However, their suicides! Sudden suicides! Until now, no one understands the real reasons? Was it economic hardship? Was it romance? No – it was neither. So what was it? It has finally become a huge question?

Similarly, both Ai Xia and Wu Jilan committed suicide! But Ai Xia attracted a lot of attention, or perhaps it could be said, sympathy. Because she was a fellow writer, she was an artist, so five or six Shanghai newspapers published special memorial issues for her, and several news reporters were troubled to personally visit her, and several newspapers used grand special headlines to report her suicide. It is said that the general literary and art circles are still preparing a memorial service for her! I think Ai Xia's death is worthwhile and glorious. She herself, even in the afterlife, would exclaim, "This death was not in vain!" Her deeds, her extraordinary deeds, may soon be compiled into books and filmed on the silver screen by great writers! After all, she is worthy of being called a "modern woman," a "daughter of the era"!

The death of the nameless glamorous corpse was by throwing herself on the Songhu Road train tracks, but what exactly happened is still unclear. Hu Zhen's death was because she was not admitted to the school she applied to. Regarding Ms. Hu's suicide, I do not want to say anything, but I think that women's minds are too narrow. For the sake of not being admitted to school, is it worth committing suicide! Although her spirit of eagerness to learn is commendable, she should not have taken such a passive path. Therefore, I dare not commend her determination to die!

Speaking of Yan Xiu'e, she was romantic in the past, and regretful later. Her final encounter was meeting an unvirtuous man, leading to abandonment. She had also received considerable education, but she went astray. Now, although she is aware of her mistakes, "one wrong step leads to eternal regret, a hundred years before you can turn back"! Originally, the temptations of money, material possessions, and sensual pleasures in this era make it easy for young women with weak wills to fall. Yan Xiu'e can serve as an excellent warning to modern young women!

I am not saying something cruel, but their deaths are not a pity. Who told them not to be good people, but instead to seek trouble? If they had used such a courageous spirit of going to their deaths to fight for their own careers! To struggle for the future of their lives! Then, I think, the final victory would belong to them. Now, they suffer the consequences of their own actions, and they cannot blame the environment, let alone society. What else is there to say?

Love—is something that is seen as nothing, smells like nothing; what is there to cherish about it? But it devours countless ambitious and promising young people, burying many in the grave of love.

Economics—Although it can control everything for people, I believe that as long as we have the same courage and perseverance as those who commit suicide to fight against it, there will come a time when it will be controlled by us.

Therefore, whether their deaths are considered great or insignificant by people, I cannot sympathize with them. I only feel sorry for them, that they died so undeservedly and so unconsciously. I am not against death, but I advocate that even death must be valuable, to be worthy of parents and society. Otherwise, it is always a misfortune for the country and a loss to society!

The tide of suicide is surging again. Taking poison in pairs, taking poison alone, the suicide cases in the future may be just beginning to flourish!

As the curtain of the 23rd year of the Republic of China has just begun to rise, shocking suicide cases have been occurring one after another in the social strata of Shanghai. In this way, I think that rather than saying that this year is the "Women's National Goods Year," it would be more accurate and more fitting to call it the "XX Suicide Year"!

Impressions After Watching the Second Public Performance of the Nameless Theater Actors Association 285

— Ling He

Compared to Chinese cinema, there is no denying that the atmosphere of stage plays is indeed frighteningly cold. Therefore, when people are eagerly hoping to obtain sufficient spiritual nourishment from the stage, even a small-scale public performance makes them feel very excited. This time, the Nameless Theater Actors Association held its second public performance at the Chen Ying Shi Memorial Hall, and on the evening of February 26th, I also went to see it with great enthusiasm.

It is said that the first public performance of the theater group was at the Jiuyai Grand Theater. At that time, because I didn't know about it, I didn't go to see it, so I naturally don't know how well it went. However, this time, although it did not give me a very good impression in terms of technique, in terms of meaning, it cannot help but make us marvel.

We can say with certainty that the members of the Nameless Theater Group, from the selection of scripts to the spirit they express, all prove that they are all strong people who are closely following the giant waves of the times and striving forward. They have a deep understanding of the current society. They deeply understand that all the old and rotten things will inevitably be destroyed, and they are eagerly looking forward to the arrival of light in their struggles and pain. Therefore, I express my sincere respect to the members of the Nameless Theater Actors Association here.

In addition, I should offer some personal opinions on this public performance in the most well-intentioned manner. Of course, this is not criticism. However, I only watched the evening performance, and what I write is limited to the four plays: "The Vagrant," "Brothers," "One Hundred Pounds," and "Three Families Living Together." At the same time, I do not want to describe each play in detail separately, but it is more convenient to speak generally.

At a time when unemployment is increasing and there is no guarantee or relief for them, "The Vagrant," which writes about social unrest and the anxiety of the unemployed from the reverse side, is naturally in line with reality. Similarly, at a time when the call for rent reduction has become widespread throughout Shanghai, the performance of "Three Families Living Together" is naturally more meaningful. In addition, "Brothers" writes about the different experiences of brothers from different environments, further unfolding the contradictory relationship of the new ethics. As for "One Hundred Pounds," perhaps we find it unfamiliar that the police officer is not concerned with the reward of one hundred pounds and releases the escaped prisoner, but the fact that revolutionary fighters have won widespread sympathy is the most obvious and common phenomenon.

In these four one-act plays, each naturally has its own individual theme, but we can easily find a common point, which is that they are very in line with reality. Social unrest, the unfortunate bloodshed and active turmoil of the oppressed, and the inevitable victorious future. What is even more obvious is that all four plays have police officers whose task is to prevent "those above from falling down and those below from turning upside down," but what they show in their actions is very ridiculous.

It is clear that these plays are not only very needed at the moment, but are also being eagerly accepted by the general audience who are struggling day and night in distress, because each play is made up of excerpts. However, the form cannot keep up with the content, which is not only the biggest regret of Chinese films, but is even more obvious in stage performance.

This is naturally undeniable, and the performance techniques undoubtedly cannot satisfy the audience's requirements. If we want to promote the progress of acting techniques, we may as well strictly put forward some necessary opinions. In "The Vagrant," the composition of the stage surface shows considerable directorial achievement. This is naturally the beautification of the set (although it cannot be more realistic). The soft lighting gives people a considerable degree of aesthetic feeling. And the grasp of the characters' positions and moods has been appropriately successful. This is not only because the vagrant has a wide space to act, but especially because the lawyer Li Peier and the tea house waiter always stand on the steps and do not come down, which is not annoying. Although the climax of the play only relies on effects, the cry of "We want bread" is ultimately tense enough to make people tremble.

Similarly, the director of "One Hundred Pounds" also saw success. Especially the silence of the deep night, from beginning to end, did not relax, which is definitely not easy to do. However, it is a pity that the appropriate lighting was not used to turn the gray cloth into the black night sky or the water surface. Especially the corner lamp on the left, like "Brothers," is completely unreasonable. If it is said that it is to help the lack of footlights, then I think it is unnecessary to consider. If there is a desolate street lamp next to the cargo box, wouldn't it be possible to illuminate the face and add a lot of mood? What's more, Spotlight gives us free use. Even if you can't see the facial expressions, it's not such a big loss in this play. Let's think about it, the beautiful moon, the desolate street lamp, the quiet piano sound, if you add the crisp sound of oars, and the wriggling figures almost turn into shadows, what kind of mood is that? However, our director is not good enough to grasp it.

Next, we should talk about "Brothers." This is a very serious tragedy. If the director can boldly emphasize the prison with dark lighting, except for the candles, there is only the faint light that penetrates from the window or the iron gate, plus the sound of iron chains, the sound of the lock when the prison door is opened and closed, and the terrible footsteps of the guards walking outside the window, wouldn't it be a poetic scene. However, an inexplicable white light shoots up from the ground. In that not-wide prison, there are such beautiful chairs and tables, regardless of whether this is a foreign custom or not, it ultimately cannot make people feel realistic. In addition, in the handling of the characters, the younger brother is always standing irrelevantly, and the older brother does not have enough opportunity to express his grief and excitement. Of course, it is because the actors' abilities are not enough, but the fact that the director did not use the actors actively cannot be denied. However, the light change in the back is still acceptable.

Finally, the worst is "Three Families Living Together." Perhaps this is because there are more people involved, making it difficult to handle, and at the same time, it is a Chinese play, making it easier for us to see the flaws in the play from our own life experiences and feelings. But the scene is completely dull, without any rhythm of the play. For example, that worker has nothing to do from beginning to end, and the others are arranged unnaturally. In particular, the atmosphere of civilized drama is too strong, which is the biggest failure. This is naturally the greatest responsibility that the director should bear.

Now we should briefly talk about some aspects of the performance. The protagonists of several plays have achieved considerable success. Jin Shanjun's role as Laure in "The Vagrant" is certainly not good enough to express the dual personality of the character in the play, but it is not a failure. Tao Haijun, who plays the lawyer in the same play, is dressed too badly. In order to exaggerate the drama, wearing a big belly must have an appropriate physique, but with his thin physique, it is a complete failure. Boss Nicholas and the mailman are quite commendable. The police officer is the worst. Ji Xujun, who plays the younger brother in "Brothers," is too unfamiliar and has no experience. Sha Baijun, who plays Annie, is okay, but still lacks composure. The makeup of the actor who plays the pastor is excellent, but unfortunately his lines are unclear. Wei Heling and Wang Ying from "One Hundred Pounds" are naturally the most skilled among all the actors. To be strict, Wang Yingjun's voice is not loud enough, and Wei Helingjun did not show the inner contradictions, and the two police officers are too weak. The roles in "Three Families Living Together" are all mediocre. Although Sha Baijun's makeup as an old woman is not very good, it is still passable. Ms. Chen Qiufang and Ms. Hu Li are both daring to act, but they are not skilled. Ji Xujun's Ah Ming and Kang Lijun's drunk are mediocre, Xu Digongjun is okay, but his lines are not familiar enough. Yao Pingjun is not enough to make people hate Diao Zhongren. Ye Mingjun is extremely unfamiliar. As for Jing Junjun

Page 20

Jing Junjun's Ah Yun was okay when she first came on stage, but later she became a completely civilized drama, and she should be the most failed one in the play.

As mentioned above, we can find a common weakness. In addition to insufficient equipment due to economic reasons, the lack of rehearsal and the hasty performance are the main reasons for the failure. As for not having a good rehearsal, the lighting or sound effects will naturally not be satisfactory. Therefore, in amateur theater groups that do not have sufficient funding, is it not a good result?

But in order to improve the technical level of drama, in order to increase the audience's interest in stage plays, in order to complete a new form to meet the requirements of the content, how will we work hard to improve our work? We demand our own theater, we demand actors who are constantly training, and we demand technical experts who take theater as a lifelong career. Therefore, we should make our best efforts to organize professional theater troupes, which is our main task at present.

The Problem of Youth Love 286

— Shou Yuan

Since the May Fourth Movement, New Romanticism has invaded this feudal China along with capitalism. As a result, young people have risen up to resist the old families, and the feudal forces have gradually been shaken by the flood of capitalism. At this time, young people are desperately struggling outward, wanting to get rid of the shackles of feudal families. They are dissatisfied with all the old morals, old etiquette, old ideas, and old literature, and are eager to seek new ideas and new literature. As a result, the literature of New Romanticism has risen! Of course, it suits the tastes of young people. The so-called "love," which China has never had before, has gradually emerged! Now it is even more common!

In today's China, which is suffering from natural disasters and man-made disasters, and internal and external troubles, anyone who understands a little feels that there is no way out for the country and individuals, and that society is dark. Warm-hearted young people naturally feel the same way! Young people with wavering wills, when they feel this way, and do not have the courage to fight in this harsh environment and find a way out, feel the oppression of evil forces, and do not have the courage to resist them, they only feel sad and troubled, so they become negative! When they can enjoy themselves, they should enjoy themselves! Live one day at a time, seek some pleasure in love! They waste their energy and time completely on love. Hypocritical love requires money to maintain. The rewards from a legitimate profession are certainly not enough to spend, so they surrender to evil forces and become lackeys!

The youth who advocate love above all else, of course, needless to say, take love as the whole of life, seeking only their own enjoyment, not knowing the past or the future. Although they sing "sacred love is unconditional"! But they will never fall in love with poor boys, they must use money as the standard. To make their love very happy, they must have money, so they also surrender to evil forces and become lackeys! Love has become the only way for young people to fall!

From the above, it seems that love is the root of youth's fall. No! Love is not a bad thing. Everyone has feelings, and it is okay to be in love at the appropriate time, but we cannot take love as the whole of life. Love is a part of human life, but the important thing is not here. The important thing is to temper ourselves, to strengthen our will. When we feel the oppression of evil forces, we should resist. When we feel that there is no way to deal with these evil forces, it is because we have not tempered ourselves well enough. So we must work hard to temper ourselves, and make ourselves sound! Then we will not just feel sad and troubled by the real problems and be unable to solve them! Nor will we become negative and fall because of trouble!

Drama

Mother (Continued) 287

— Ke Xin

Poor woman (stands up from the wall)... I can't bear... to watch you... in my arms... this living... starve... to death... She hangs her head, choked with sobs, and struggles toward the "infant receiving station." When she gets there, she can't support herself. She is leaning on the wall near that drawer with one hand. After resting for a while, she straightens up and looks at that monster-like drawer, reaching out her trembling hand to pull the drawer open. As soon as she touches it, she shrinks back as if she had been electrocuted, tightly holding the baby, afraid that her treasure will be sucked away or harmed. She turns her back and leans against the wall.

At this time, the cold gradually rises, and the snowflakes fall more densely. She shields her baby from the wind and snow, but the wind always attacks her, and the snow always accumulates on her. She is shivering from the cold and can't resist it. Poor woman (takes off her headscarf and covers the baby's head), I can't... let you... freeze to death... in my... arms...

Shivering, she turns around again, timidly approaching the drawer. Just as she is about to reach out to open it...

Baby, guā, guā, guā...

The poor woman quickly retracts her hand and leans against the wall, her head buried in her hands, her back to the audience. She is sobbing, and her shoulders are moving with the baby's cries.

The baby's cries gradually weaken and finally stop. At this time, the wind is stronger and the snow is denser. The poor woman does not turn around, but nervously and tremblingly reaches out to grope for the drawer. She gropes for the drawer handle and grabs it tightly, letting her hand tremble violently there for a while. The drawer slowly opens. She still holds the handle tightly and tremblingly, gradually turning around, looking at the drawer. As she looks at it, the drawer seems to have become a terrible monster's bloody mouth, and she quickly closes it. Tightly holding her child.

Poor woman: I can't, I can't...

She leaves the drawer and wants to go back, but her heavy feet are heavier than when she came, and it is more and more difficult to drag them. Finally, she stops.

Poor woman: Go back... go back... what will I use to raise... my baby? You want to live, you can't; if we have the chance in the future, we will still... baby, I'm not abandoning you... You can't blame me, baby... baby...

As she speaks, she walks toward the drawer. While reaching out to open the drawer, she kisses the baby passionately, sobbing and shouting, until she puts the baby in the drawer and does not stop.

Poor woman (face leaving the baby): Baby, baby...

Sobbing, shouting, slowly pushing the drawer. Finally, she closes it suddenly. She sobs even more fiercely as she is lying there.

Poor woman (inside, suddenly): Guā, guā...

The baby's cries gradually recede.

Poor woman (hurriedly wakes up, pulls open the drawer, sees that it is empty, and anxiously) Baby; baby...

The baby's cries gradually weaken, but the poor woman's voice gradually becomes louder and more urgent.

The wind is blowing fast, and the snow is falling fast. The violin tune now hurts people's hearts as if it is gouging them out.

Poor woman: Baby, baby...

She finally can't support herself, collapsing under the drawer in a heap of grief.

The cold wind sweeps her disheveled hair, and the dense snow rushes to gather on her. The violin seems to be mourning for her with sympathy.

Film Special

"Storm Over Mexico" 288

— Xu Xingzhi

(1) The Making Process and Disputes

Back in 1930, when Sergei Eisenstein was trying to make his first sound film in Paris, he happened to meet Duca from Paramount Pictures. Duca admired Eisenstein's reputation and immediately asked him to come to Hollywood to make a film. After Eisenstein returned to his country, he brought up the matter for discussion. Having obtained the agreement of his compatriots, Eisenstein, with the mission of absolutely not compromising on "content" and "theme," came to Hollywood to join Paramount Pictures. Initially, the two or three scripts proposed by Eisenstein did not suit the taste of Paramount's producers in any way. Later, with "An American Tragedy," he obtained Duca's consent and started filming. Unfortunately, it was stopped again by an order from the authorities saying "Absolutely no filming allowed."

However, with the help of his friend Upton Sinclair, Eisenstein started a new project, which was the famous "Storm Over Mexico" (Thunder Over Mexico), which stirred up waves in the global film industry. This new project was directed by Eisenstein, scripted by F.G. Alexandrov, and photographed by Eduard Tisse. From 1931 to 1932, it took eleven months, used 200,000 feet of film, and was divided into five parts, with the past, present, and future of Mexico as the themes, creating a narrative poem of Mexican history. However, on the one hand, Sinclair ran out of money and withdrew midway, and on the other hand, Eisenstein had to return to his country for personal reasons, leaving all the film footage in the bustling Hollywood. However, Sinclair, a speculator, for the sake of commercial gain, cut and spliced 7,000 feet of film from the 200,000 feet of film, selected less than one-fifth of the original work's material, and skillfully used Eisenstein's name to publicly sell it in the 1933 film market.

Therefore, the disputes and repercussions caused in the film city of America also stirred up a great storm, coinciding with the title. First, understanding film practitioners and critics began to protest, such as Rover, a strong supporter of Eisenstein in Mexico. Following this movement, the members of the American "Experimental Cinema" magazine organized the "Eisenstein Mexico Film Association," believing that "Storm Over Mexico" was a vulgar and evil film that damaged Eisenstein's reputation, and launched a movement to ban its public screening. Then, the June and September issues of "Closeup" magazine published a declaration, supporting the film that Eisenstein shot in Mexico. They stated that if it was not a work edited by Eisenstein himself, it should not be called a finished film, and proposed a movement to return all the film footage to Eisenstein. Later, famous film critics such as Pound and Braver-Mann were also drawn into the vortex of this event. In particular, on July 5th of last year, Sinclair even issued a statement regarding "Storm Over Mexico," saying, "This was edited according to Eisenstein's intentions." Afterwards, many opinions and groups were discovered, and Eisenstein experts appeared. According to recent rumors, Sinclair was on the verge of bankruptcy because of this film, and Eisenstein was about to file a lawsuit against Sinclair to protect his reputation. Therefore, the waves in the film industry caused by this film became even more chaotic and expanded further.

Film Review

Review of "His Double Life" Litt—Da Guangming 289

— Ling He

In this hypocritical society of idol worship, artists, with their keen senses, feel most deeply about their own works being misunderstood or even given incorrect evaluations. Artists consider this to be the greatest pain. In their eyes, the general ignorant appreciators do not necessarily understand the true value of art. However, when a small number of artists become famous, their works will be considered priceless treasures. At this time, cunning merchants profit from it, making rash criticisms with their superficial understanding, and art becomes a commodity, and the artist suffers from then on.

We have read countless similar works of art in novels or dramas. The recently released "Heart's Desire" also ridiculed and scolded this situation. And this "His Double Life," adapted from a novel, is an even more delightful scolding.

I don't think this needs further explanation. The death of a famous painter's servant can be mistaken for the painter's death, shocking the whole country, while the painter himself is ridiculed and even driven away by the police as a madman. Similarly, art merchants boldly use the painter's name to make a lot of money. Strange things happen one after another, and jokes pile up. Thus, the pure and straightforward painter, in his sadness, concludes that ignorant and cunning people all wear shameful masks, and he himself is unreasonably being toyed with.

We cannot help but be moved by the subject matter described above. However, the performance techniques appear very mediocre. If we were to be more demanding, then it is simply, apart from some humorous dialogue, nothing to commend.

Of course, we are saying that with American film technology, it should have been more successful. But the director, in addition to narrating this bizarre and tortuous story, did not emphasize the story more dramatically. We only see Laurel and Hardy doing quite a bit of acting, while Liliane Haidee, who plays the female lead, simply has nothing to do. The whole film is dull, obscure, like the plum rain season, making people feel weak and bored to death. Perhaps we will not overlook the simple techniques in it, such as Alice and Fred starting to live together, ending with just saying "I do" to each other, but when Alice meets Rick's wife, it is a long conversation around the table. Fortunately, the obscure atmosphere is considerably harmonized by funny words. When Rick and his mother left, the scene of Fred walking into the house from the heavy night fog was very beautiful. Later, the scene of washing feet, that sketch of a harmonious family, is also very commendable. Furthermore, the masks on everyone's faces in Fred's eyes should be the deepest intention of this film. However, some parts of the court are operatic, which is very inconsistent with the realistic style of the whole film.

What else is there to say? Liliane Haidee gave the Chinese audience the most painful impression. Therefore, her dubbed version of Griffith's famous work "Marriage License?" was once released, and her name is quite appealing in China. However, the glory of the past has ultimately faded with her youth. Here, although she is dressed as a young girl, she cannot hide the inherent twilight in her movements and expressions. However, why did she, who is known for playing tragedies, play this non-crying and non-smiling role when she re-emerged on the screen? She is indeed a typical role of a virtuous wife and loving mother, but unfortunately, she has not fully played it here. I think this should be the director's fault. On the contrary, Laurel and Hardy, who are usually known for playing quirky roles, have achieved considerable success in playing a loyal and docile painter here.

Film Novel Iron-Blooded Rose (4) 294

— Long Geng

Gao Yan told Xuejuan that Zhenxiao was just outside the door, how happy Xuejuan would be! She only felt that her heart was pouring hot blood into her whole body, but, after all, this could not become a reality. Zhenxiao was indeed outside the door, but he was tightly bound by soldiers. He was a serious criminal. Xuejuan's heart was filled with happiness, but at this moment, it was immediately driven away by horror. She wanted to rush forward, she wanted to throw herself into Zhenxiao's arms, she was crazy, she shouted crazily...

Under Gao Yan's hint, Lu Yuanfu groped for his pistol, preparing to shoot Lin Zhenxiao. —He had run close to Zhenxiao and covered his eyes with a handkerchief for him.

Xuejuan jumped wildly, like a carp being fried in a pot of oil, like... "Bang!" As the gunshot rang, Xuejuan fell into Gao Yan's arms, she fainted.

Gao Yan felt victorious! Laughed! —That smile was too ugly!

Just as Gao Yan's lips were approaching Xuejuan's — the lips of this fainted Xuejuan, suddenly, Xuejuan woke up, using her fists, hard, hard like a thunderous storm, she wildly knocked and beat Gao Yan's chest, knowing that this could not save her dead husband, but a feeling of "pain and anger" drove her to act so crazily. Of course, Gao Yan would not be angry, victory already completely belonged to him.

Xuejuan discovered the pistol on the table and immediately rushed forward to grab it, angrily, she pulled, pulled,... ah!

There were no bullets! Gao Yan on the other side looked at her and laughed!

While Xuejuan was trying to load the bullets, Gao Yan suddenly came over, tightly hugging her, preparing to enjoy her. Of course, Xuejuan was struggling, struggling, desperately struggling...

Suddenly, Gao Yan fell to the ground and died with a gunshot. Xuejuan was extremely surprised! When her suspicious gaze was released, Zhenxiao, —the Zhenxiao who had been shot, appeared outside the door led by Lu Yuanfu.

Not dead? Yes, Zhenxiao was not dead, Lu Yuanfu only fired a blank shot. So, Xuejuan laughed! At the same time, Zhenxiao and Yuanfu's hands were tightly, tightly, tightly held together.

The sound of knocking on the door was fierce. Lu Yuanfu wanted the pistol that Zhenxiao used to kill Gao Yan, had Zhenxiao put on Gao Yan's clothes, and led Xuejuan to escape.

When the door was knocked open, this repentant Yuanfu confessed that he was the murderer. He wanted to redeem his past sins with a spirit of great sacrifice, although he knew this was not enough.

On the one hand, Zhenxiao and Xuejuan embarked on the great road of revolution that they had long yearned for in their hearts. They said: "...It is useless to kill one Gao Yan, this is the whole problem." (End)
